Pro: Female suffrage was not given in any European country [before 1906](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false).
1.1.3.1.2.2. Pro: There was a [class biased](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) suffrage system based on tax contribution that excluded the underprivileged.
1.1.3.1.2.2.1. Pro: In France [99%](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) of males were discriminated against due to tax based voting systems before 1848.
1.1.3.1.2.2.2. Pro: At the time a suffrage system based on tax contribution was judged as good because more rich people were represented.
1.1.3.1.2.2.2.1. Pro: In Prussia and Russia, it was judged that [wealthy people](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) are more important to the state and thus should be allowed to have more influence.
1.1.3.1.2.2.2.2. Pro: Across the continent it was generally held that [poor people](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) are stupid and thus should be not equally represented in elections.
1.1.3.1.2.2.2.3. Pro: It was [common knowledge](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) at that time that only the wealthy would have sufficient leisure time to consider political options and thus are in a position to make adequate decisions.
1.1.3.1.2.2.2.4. Pro: [Arguments](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) were made that the wealthy are more disinterested from gains from the state than the poor and thus are more ethical in their decisions.
1.1.3.1.2.2.3. Pro: Voting for Lower Legislation Chambers typically was only possible if a man possessed [sufficient property](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false).
1.1.3.1.2.2.4. Pro: In [19th century Spain](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false), only around 20% of the population was allowed to vote.
1.1.3.1.2.3. Pro: [Indirect voting](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) through electors was prevalent to ensure that only 'well-known' candidates would be eligible for the legislature.
1.1.3.1.2.3.1. Con: This in itself is not undemocratic as the same system was applied in the [US](http://press.uchicago.edu/ucp/books/book/chicago/W/bo11315021.html) and transformed quickly because these electors had no independent power.
1.1.3.1.2.4. Pro: High minimum [age threshold](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) excluded a significant part of the population. Typically it was set at 25.
1.1.3.1.2.5. Con: There were restrictions on suffrage rights during the 1990s as well.
1.1.3.1.2.5.1. Pro: In some countries not all convicted criminals could vote.
1.1.3.1.2.5.1.1. Pro: In the [United Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felony_disenfranchisement#United_Kingdom), incarcerated criminals got excluded from suffrage rights.
1.1.3.1.2.5.1.2. Pro: In [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felony_disenfranchisement#United_Kingdom), the most serious offenses involved the loss of voting rights.
1.1.3.1.2.5.1.3. Pro: In [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felony_disenfranchisement#United_Kingdom), upon special court order only, those convicted of electoral fraud and crimes undermining the democratic order are barred from voting while in prison.
1.1.3.1.2.5.2. Pro: It was considered unconstitutional for the [British Sovereign](https://www.royal.gov.uk/MonarchUK/QueenandGovernment/Queenandvoting.aspx) and his or her heir to vote.
1.1.3.1.2.5.3. Pro: The citizens of [Gibraltar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matthews_v_United_Kingdom) were excluded from voting for the European Parliament in the 1990s.
1.1.3.1.2.6. Pro: French army [personnel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suffrage#Function) was prohibited from voting.
1.1.3.1.3. Pro: The freedom of press was limited and therewith prevented adequate policy discussions.
1.1.3.1.3.1. Pro: [Censorship](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) was widespread and therewith limited political expression.
1.1.3.1.3.2. Pro: [Newspapers](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) were often obliged to pay special taxes or deposit securities so they would not violate state interests. This encouraged self-censorship.
1.1.3.1.3.3. Pro: The vagueness of censorship laws induced [self-censorship](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) because journalists could not be aware of what was acceptable.
1.1.3.1.4. Pro: Assembly and association rights were [restricted](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false), which favored the status quo.
1.1.3.1.5. Pro: Strikes and trade unions were restricted which aggravated the ply of labor.
1.1.3.1.5.1. Pro: In Italy, Spain, Portugal, Hungary and Russia it was not legal to form a trade [union](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) until the early 20th century.
1.1.3.1.5.2. Pro: Most [European](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) countries even after liberalization did not grant meaningful freedom of union activities by continued harassment.
1.1.3.1.6. Pro: Secret police techniques were widespread to silence dissidents.
1.1.3.1.6.1. Pro: '[Dirty tricks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dirty_tricks)' were widespread in [19th century Europe](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false).
1.1.3.1.6.2. Pro: Public [surveillance](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) made it dangerous to talk about the state publicly.
1.1.3.1.6.3. Pro: Secret police sent agents abroad to spy on the [political opposition](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) living in exile.
1.1.3.1.7. Pro: Academic freedom was [limited](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) to induce a certain way of thinking.
1.1.3.1.8. Con: After the 1870s, lower classes were able to gain a certain degree of [political influence](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=zYLR_ewddRoC&pg=PA100&lpg=PA100&dq=average+stores+19th+century+euro&source=bl&ots=-qhsKAoozy&sig=By4I_-DV0DkyLqUVGxhPDnrc6BY&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjyy4rnupvLAhUBwZQKHTYVApgQ6AEIKzAC#v=onepage&q&f=false).
1.1.3.2. Con: -> See 1.1.1.5.2.
1.1.3.3. Con: Globalization made it even harder for states to actually enforce their laws, for example against [transnational criminality](http://www.cfr.org/transnational-crime/globalization-affects-transnational-crime/p28403) \(trafficking, smuggling\) and [tax evasion](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=2KZQabqIOkoC&pg=PR4&dq=Tax+Havens:+How+Globalization+Really+Works&hl=en&sa=X&redir_esc=y#v=onepage&q&f=false).
1.1.3.4. Con: Crime rates increased in Europe between the 1890s and 1990s.
1.1.3.4.1. Con: [Homicide rates](http://ourworldindata.org/data/violence-rights/homicides/) have declined since 1890 making society safer for individuals.
1.1.3.4.1.1. Con: Homicide rates in [England and Wales](http://researchbriefings.parliament.uk/ResearchBriefing/Summary/RP99-111#fullreport) increased between 1900 and 1997.
1.1.3.4.1.1.1. Con: We need to keep our sight on the word "Europe" - statistics for some fairly small regions are useless at best and manipulative at worst. \("Fairly small" compared to the accepted geographical definition of Europe as stretching from the Urals to the North Pole to Malta, etc.\)
1.1.3.4.1.2. Pro: Violence has been declining since the 1890s, as is evident in the development of [homicide rates](https://ourworldindata.org/homicides/) in major European countries which halved.
1.1.3.4.1.2.1. Con: Statistics show that there has been a [U-shaped pattern](http://www.vrc.crim.cam.ac.uk/vrcresearch/paperdownload/manuel-eisner-historical-trends-in-violence.pdf) in terms of European homicide rates that saw them decreasing from the late 19th century until 1950, and once again rising until the end of the 20th century.
1.1.3.4.2. Pro: In the [UK](https://www.gov.uk/government/statistics/historical-crime-data) the number of cases of violence across all sections rose by a factor of 30 between the 1890s and the 1990s even though the population only grew by 1.5.
1.1.3.4.2.1. Pro: Cases of [violence](https://www.gov.uk/government/statistics/historical-crime-data) against a person rose from 2,144 in 1898 to 256,000 in 1989.
1.1.3.4.2.2. Pro: The number of total [sexual offences](https://www.gov.uk/government/statistics/historical-crime-data) increased from 1,723 in 1898 to 34,000 in 1989.
1.1.3.4.2.3. Pro: The number of cases involving [theft or burglary](https://www.gov.uk/government/statistics/historical-crime-data) increased from 63,000 in 1898 to 2,144,000 in 1989.
1.1.3.4.2.4. Con: The source explicitly states that these numbers "are affected by changes in levels of reporting to the police and recording by them". They might thus say little about actual crime rates.
1.1.3.4.2.4.1. Con: The crimes rates increased by a factor of 30 or more. This means that to offset the crime levels crime reporting would have to improve by a similar factor.
1.1.3.4.2.4.1.1. Pro: Despite significant technological improvements between [1973 and 2005](http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/j.1745-9125.2010.00182.x/abstract) the crime reporting rate increased not even by a factor of 2. Thus we can estimate that the changes will not reach a magnitude of 30 between the 1890s and the 1990s.
1.1.3.4.2.5. Pro: Even if adjusted for [population growth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demography_of_the_United_Kingdom#UK_population_change_over_time) which doubled between 1900 and 2000 the increases are still stronger than population increases.
1.1.3.4.3. Pro: The number of [recorded crimes](https://chs.revues.org/989) increased drastically since the 1890s.
1.1.3.4.3.1. Con: Recording of crime rates can increase due to factors unrelated to actual violence, such as more trust in the police or better recording systems.
1.1.3.4.4. Pro: Criminality levels of [theft and violence](http://jessnevins.com/blog/?p=89) have been dramatically reduced by the 1890s already. Thus, no major change in individual security is observable by the 1990s.
1.1.3.5. Pro: With Human Rights there was a minimum standard introduced to rely upon.
1.1.3.6. Pro: Humanitarian law was introduced, giving individual protection even in times of war.
1.1.4. Pro: The abolishment of monarchies improved many peoples' lives.
1.1.4.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.1.
1.1.4.2. Pro: Legal developments led to a more equal society and thus profited Europeans' life.
1.1.4.2.1. Pro: Equal rights improved womens' quality of life.
1.1.4.2.1.1. Pro: Women could decide independently if they want to work.
1.1.4.2.1.1.1. Pro: Women increasingly have entered the [labor market](https://books.google.co.kr/books?hl=en&lr=&id=U8Du1ErYPC0C&oi=fnd&pg=PR1&dq=reproductive+work+women+europe&ots=r73z1zecV2&sig=wCVQdFRyqPSs61cAjl_OziOvVIA#v=onepage&q=reproductive%20work%20women%20europe&f=false) since 1900.
1.1.4.2.1.2. Pro: Women could choose if they want to have children.
1.1.4.2.1.2.1. Pro: The invention of the birth control pill in the 1960s improved family planning and strenghtened womens' rights by giving them control over their fertility.
1.1.4.2.1.2.1.1. Pro: [Side effects](http://www.glowm.com/section_view/item/375) of the Pill reduced during the 20th century.
1.1.4.2.1.2.2. Pro: Women could get abortions legally.
1.1.4.2.1.2.2.1. Pro: This severely lowered the health risks of unsafe illegal abortions.
1.1.4.2.1.2.2.2. Pro: Abortions in most European countries were [illegal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abortion_law) in the 19th century.
1.1.4.2.1.2.2.2.1. Pro: According to Art 218 Reichsstrafgesetzbuch, in Prussia abortion was illegal after 1871.
1.1.4.2.1.2.2.2.2. Pro: Abortions in the [UK](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malicious_Shooting_or_Stabbing_Act_1803) were made illegal in the beginning of the 19th century.
1.1.4.2.1.2.2.2.3. Pro: Making women criminals for having an abortion is bad for their mental health.
1.1.4.2.1.2.2.2.3.1. Con: In [France](http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/11614490) the notion was thought of a thinkable solution for unwanted pregnancy.
1.1.4.2.1.3. Pro: Women got full voting rights which enabled them to participate politically.
1.1.4.2.1.4. Con: Through the equality movement, women have experienced a reduction in the quality of life.
1.1.4.2.1.4.1. Pro: With the right to work, women do experience [double burdens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_burden) of commercial and domestic work.
1.1.4.2.1.4.1.1. Con: On average, women and men across Europe perform the same total number of productive work hours. The idea of double burden is a [myth](http://www.lse.ac.uk/newsAndMedia/news/archives/2010/08/CatherineHakimRenewal.pdf).
1.1.4.2.1.4.1.2. Pro: The [double burden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_burden#Health_effects) of women increases women's stress level, the mortality rate, the work intensity and a loss in sleep.
1.1.4.2.1.4.1.3. Con: The double burden results from the lack of childcare institutions, not from womens' right to work.
1.1.4.2.1.4.1.3.1. Pro: In Europe the main reason for women to abstain from a full time position is the [need to take care](http://s3.amazonaws.com/zanran_storage/stuwww.uvt.nl/ContentPages/51710139.pdf) of children and the elderly.
1.1.4.2.1.4.1.3.2. Con: What seems to be successful in [Sweden](http://europa.eu/epic/countries/sweden/index_en.htm) is flexible parental leave and not the provision of childcare institutions.
1.1.4.2.1.4.2. Pro: Women increasingly participated in warfare activities of men.
1.1.4.2.1.4.2.1. Pro: It was since the Crimean War that [nursing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_nursing) became increasingly widespread through the activities of Florence Nightingale.
1.1.4.2.1.4.2.2. Pro: In the two World Wars it became established that [women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_the_World_Wars) contribute to war efforts through work in factories.
1.1.4.2.1.4.2.3. Pro: Female combat participation became a possible scenario for many societies.
1.1.4.2.1.4.2.3.1. Pro: In [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_World_War_II) female participation in combat activities became widespread across the continent.
1.1.4.2.1.4.2.3.2. Pro: Initial steps for female participation in warfare were laid in [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_World_War_I).
1.1.4.2.1.4.2.3.3. Pro: The 20th century saw the gradual expansion of possibilities for regular [female service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_the_military_by_country#Europe) in the armed forces across the continent.
1.1.4.2.1.4.2.3.3.1. Con: Women are not allowed to join the [special forces](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/tvandradio/11832806/Action-woman-puts-male-competitors-to-shame-in-gruelling-Special-Forces-training.html) in the UK.
1.1.4.2.1.4.2.3.3.2. Con: Military service is not bad for women who decide for themselves that they want to do it.
1.1.4.2.1.5. Con: In many aspects of gender equality not much has changed between 1890 and 1990.
1.1.4.2.1.5.1. Pro: Of those who lived in [poverty](http://www.helsinki.fi/science/xantippa/wle/wle13.html) 70% were women. Thus, it is still women who suffer most.
1.1.4.2.1.5.2. Pro: Equal rights have changed little about the gender pay [gap](http://www.equalityhumanrights.com/sites/default/files/documents/research/gender_pay_gap_briefing_paper2.pdf).
1.1.4.2.1.5.3. Pro: [The perception](http://gender-competence.eu/files/IntConf/5.pdf) of mothers in employment as less caring for their children has changed little with advances in legal rights.
1.1.4.2.1.6. Pro: Full-time working mothers in 1995 spend as much [time](http://www.soc.umn.edu/~elkelly/Bianchietal2000HouseworkTrends.pdf) with their children as part-time employed mothers in 1975. More equality with their husbands has allowed them for this.
1.1.4.2.1.7. Pro: Socialism improved the rights of women dramatically and positioned them well in society by 1990s.
1.1.4.2.1.7.1. Pro: Women's participation in the workforce in [socialist systems](http://www.amazon.com/Democratic-Transition-Slovenia-Transformation-Education/dp/1585445258) was very high by 1990.
1.1.4.2.1.8. Pro: The [Vienna Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vienna_Declaration_and_Programme_of_Action) and Programme of Action from 1993 recognized [women's rights](http://www.ohchr.org/Documents/ProfessionalInterest/vienna.pdf) as being protected human rights.
1.1.4.2.1.8.1. Con: The European Convention on Human Rights has more favorable conditions and was signed earlier. Thus, the Vienna Declaration \([VDPA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vienna_Declaration_and_Programme_of_Action)\) of 1993 made no difference for the life of Europeans.
1.1.4.2.1.8.1.1. Con: Even though the provisions were stricter there was no actual ruling [before 1993](http://www.echr.coe.int/Documents/FS_Domestic_violence_ENG.pdf).
1.1.4.2.1.8.1.2. Con: The VDPA explicitly recognises gender-based violence, sexual harassment and exploitation and proclaims women's rights as legitimate issues for the international community.
1.1.4.2.1.8.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.2.1.8.1.2.
1.1.4.2.1.9. Pro: Women could become priests.
1.1.4.2.1.9.1. Pro: [Ordination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ordination_of_women_in_Protestant_churches) of women has been taking place in an increasing number of Protestant churches during the 20th century.
1.1.4.2.1.9.2. Pro: The ordination of women in the [Anglican](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ordination_of_women_in_the_Anglican_Communion) Communion has been increasingly common in certain provinces since the 1970s.
1.1.4.2.1.9.3. Con: Due to the Catholic Church doctrine on the [ordination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church_doctrine_on_the_ordination_of_women) of women, women cannot be ordained.
1.1.4.2.1.9.4. Pro: There was no [ordained women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_women's_ordination) in Europe before the 20th century.
1.1.4.2.1.10. Pro: Womens' [property rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_women%27s_rights_\(other_than_voting\)#1900.E2.80.931939) were more advanced by the 1990s in all European countries.
1.1.4.2.1.11. Pro: Gender equality in parental rights over children was introduced in all European countries.
1.1.4.2.1.11.1. Con: [Child custody rights](https://www.princeton.edu/futureofchildren/publications/journals/article/index.xml?journalid=63&articleid=414&sectionid=2825) that favored women were evolving rapidly at the turn of the century already.
1.1.4.2.1.12. Pro: [Marital rape](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marital_rape) was made illegal.
1.1.4.2.1.13. Pro: Women could go to university in all European countries.
1.1.4.2.1.13.1. Con: Women had access to tertiary education in the 1890s.
1.1.4.2.1.13.1.1. Pro: The Swedish [Royal Seminary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Seminary) was the first female higher education institute and was founded in 1861.
1.1.4.2.1.13.1.2. Pro: In 1883 [Ellen Fries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ellen_Fries) showed that it is possible to earn a PhD even if one is a woman.
1.1.4.2.1.13.1.3. Pro: [Sofia Kovalevskaya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sofia_Kovalevskaya) became the first female Professor in 1889.
1.1.4.2.1.14. Pro: Divorce law was liberalized.
1.1.4.2.2. Pro: Children born to unmarried parents were considered "bastards" back in the 1890s.
1.1.4.2.2.1. Pro: For example in Great Britain so-called "[bastards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bastard_%28law_of_England_and_Wales%29)" could not inherit in the intestancy of his parents up until 1969.
1.1.4.2.2.2. Pro: It was in 1975 that the European Convention on the Legal Status of [illegitimate children](http://www.coe.int/en/web/conventions/full-list/-/conventions/treaty/085) was agreed upon, trying to improve the legal status of illegitimate children. It was signed by European countries such as Denmark, Greece, Ireland, Austria and Switzerland.
1.1.4.2.3. Pro: The live of minorities improved legally, socially, politically and health wise.
1.1.4.2.3.1. Con: Europe was more decentralized in the 1890s which supported the life of local minorities because they were able to live in their communities.
1.1.4.2.3.1.1. Pro: The voice of minorities was more influential because the communities were smaller.
1.1.4.2.3.1.1.1. Pro: In small communities opinions of the small minority are more likely to be consistent since the group size is smaller. This makes minority groups more influential.
1.1.4.2.3.1.1.2. Pro: The relative weight of minorities in small communities is greater.
1.1.4.2.3.1.1.2.1. Pro: Sorbs in the city of [Lohsa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lohsa) were the majority in the 19th century but turned into a minority in the 20th century. This reduced their influence.
1.1.4.2.3.1.1.3. Pro: Minorities might stretch across frontiers. Decentralized decisions prevent decisions based on a national basis.
1.1.4.2.3.1.1.3.1. Pro: The German centralized [government](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=sH5qCgAAQBAJ&pg=PA54&lpg=PA54&dq=lohsa+sorbs&source=bl&ots=DArt6edxUv&sig=ndCbv-h4cZqkWCmc0zgWRscIqTk&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjRmIzFuJvLAhXmJaYKHagjCJoQ6AEIMTAF#v=onepage&q&f=false) in the 19th century pressured Saxonia to cut back on the minority status of Sorbs.
1.1.4.2.3.1.1.4. Con: In the 1890s, the unifying forces of nation-making were much stronger than in the 1990s. This marginalized the interests of minorities.
1.1.4.2.3.1.1.4.1. Pro: After the 1870 unification of Germany there was a strong [Germanization pressure](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=sH5qCgAAQBAJ&pg=PA54&lpg=PA54&dq=lohsa+sorbs&source=bl&ots=DArt6edxUv&sig=ndCbv-h4cZqkWCmc0zgWRscIqTk&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjRmIzFuJvLAhXmJaYKHagjCJoQ6AEIMTAF#v=onepage&q&f=false) on minorities, such as the Sorbs.
1.1.4.2.3.1.2. Pro: [Centralization](http://journals.cambridge.org/action/displayAbstract?fromPage=online&aid=3894544) was, even in established nation states, not very far by the mid 19th century.
1.1.4.2.3.1.3. Con: Decentralization allows discrimination to be underreported because there is no big information community.
1.1.4.2.3.2. Pro: The disability rights movement contributed to an understanding of people with disabilities \(including not to be called 'disabled'\) as a minority or a coalition of minorities who are disadvantaged by society, not just as people who are disadvantaged by their impairments.
1.1.4.2.3.2.1. Con: For people with disabilities, disadvantages in society result from disadvantages by their impariments.
1.1.4.2.3.2.2. Pro: The [disability rights movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_disability_rights_outside_the_United_States) only arose in the second half of the 20th century.
1.1.4.2.3.2.3. Pro: Persons with disabilities were only able to achieve major rights [improvements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timeline_of_disability_rights_outside_the_United_States) for rights of persons with disabilities after the 1970s.
1.1.4.2.3.2.4. Pro: Since the 1970s, people with [epilepsy](http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1046/j.1528-1157.44.s.6.2.x/pdf) are allowed to marry in the UK.
1.1.4.2.3.2.5. Pro: Improvements in inclusion made life easier for people with disabilities.
1.1.4.2.3.3. Pro: The situation for age minorities improved.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1. Pro: Various local and international statutes were put in place to mitigate the exploitation of children, such as the Convention on the Rights of the Child, as well as a number of organizations that make up the children's rights movement.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1. Con: The Convention on the Rights of the Child had no effect to improve the living conditions of children in Europe.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.1. Pro: European countries failed to establish national [ombudspersons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Children%27s_Ombudsman) for the right of children in the 1990s.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.2. Pro: It took [until the 2000s](http://www.unicef-irc.org/publications/pdf/CRC_Impact_summaryreport.pdf) that Germany recognized the right of children to a non-violent upbringing.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.3. Pro: Corporal punishment was not made illegal in Romania [until 2004](http://www.unicef-irc.org/publications/pdf/CRC_Impact_summaryreport.pdf).
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.4. Pro: During the 1990s the UK has kept opt-outs of the [Children Rights Convention](http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/uk_news/politics/7624450.stm) that discriminate against migrant children.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.5. Con: The convention has harmonized legislative processes among European countries.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.5.1. Pro: The [convention](https://www.unicef-irc.org/publications/pdf/CRC_Impact_summaryreport.pdf) has been implemented into national law by European states.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.5.2. Pro: All over Europe independent children rights institutions have been established following the [convention](https://www.unicef-irc.org/publications/pdf/CRC_Impact_summaryreport.pdf).
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.6. Con: The convention has standardized the conception that children have rights in Europe.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.6.1. Pro: Other than the [convention](http://www.echr.coe.int/Documents/Handbook_rights_child_ENG.pdf) there is no European wide legal definition of what constitutes a child.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.6.2. Pro: All attempts of the EU and the Council of Europe to provide for children laws were piecemeal in the 1990s. Thus the convention served as a lowest common [denominator](http://www.echr.coe.int/Documents/Handbook_rights_child_ENG.pdf).
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.6.3. Pro: The European Court of Human Rights ruled that the [convention](http://hudoc.echr.coe.int/eng?i=001-61194#{"itemid":\["001-61194"\]}) sets the minimum standard all European governments have to adhere to.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.7. Con: The convention has led to clear revisions of national laws.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.7.1. Pro: After implementation the Czech constitutional court ruled certain provision of [national family law](https://www.unicef-irc.org/publications/pdf/CRC_Impact_summaryreport.pdf) as incompatible and therewith invalid.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.7.2. Pro: Legislation on [adoption](https://www.unicef-irc.org/publications/pdf/CRC_Impact_summaryreport.pdf) has been modified or replaced by new laws in most of the countries of Central and Eastern Europe.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.7.3. Pro: Eastern European countries have made [extensive changes](https://www.unicef-irc.org/publications/pdf/CRC_Impact_summaryreport.pdf) to their legislation concerning family care.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.7.4. Pro: In Poland, Sweden and Romania new legislation concerning the rights of children to [health](https://www.unicef-irc.org/publications/pdf/CRC_Impact_summaryreport.pdf) have been enacted.
1.1.4.2.3.3.1.1.7.5. Pro: In many European countries education has been reformed to acknowledge for [children rights](https://www.unicef-irc.org/publications/pdf/CRC_Impact_summaryreport.pdf).

1.1.4.2.3.3.2. Con: The elderly, while traditionally influential or even \(in a gerontocracy\) dominant in the past, have in the modern age usually been reduced to the minority role of economically 'non-active' groups.
1.1.4.2.3.3.2.1. Con: The elderly were still a valuable age group for most political parties in th 1990s.
1.1.4.2.3.3.2.1.1. Pro: The elderly are a valuable age group for political parties because of demographic changes in the [1990s](https://populationpyramid.net/europe/1997/).
1.1.4.2.3.4. Pro: Respect for the rights of persons belonging to minorities is one of the [values](http://ec.europa.eu/justice/fundamental-rights/minorities/index_en.htm) of the EU.
1.1.4.2.3.4.1. Con: Minorities in France do not have any particular [cultural status](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=Cp8tCgAAQBAJ&pg=PA228&lpg=PA228&dq=france+minority+rights+european+human+rights&source=bl&ots=uok4U7JF2b&sig=9qZot1t2XkSo2wjyfcoROqed0n0&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwiVz8bz3pTLAhVk36YKHdsrCjAQ6AEIMjAD#v=onepage&q&f=false) granting special rights next to those applicable for all citizens.
1.1.4.2.3.4.1.1. Pro: France made a [reservation](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=Cp8tCgAAQBAJ&pg=PA228&lpg=PA228&dq=france+minority+rights+european+human+rights&source=bl&ots=uok4U7JF2b&sig=9qZot1t2XkSo2wjyfcoROqed0n0&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwiVz8bz3pTLAhVk36YKHdsrCjAQ6AEIMjAD#v=onepage&q=france&f=false) to the International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights because it feared implementation of its minority provisions.
1.1.4.2.3.4.2. Con: In light of Roma and Sinti, not much has changed since 1890.
1.1.4.2.3.4.2.1. Pro: In 1886 Bismark expelled Roma and Sinti because of the "[mischief caused by families of Gypsies](http://www.radoc.net/radoc.php?doc=art_b_history_rootsofprejudice&lang=en&articles=true)".  By 1990 they were still [targets](http://hatecrime.osce.org/what-hate-crime/bias-against-roma-and-sinti) of violent attacks all over Europe.
1.1.4.2.3.4.2.2. Pro: The end of communism has worsened the [situation](https://www.kluwerlawonline.com/abstract.php?area=Journals&id=EURO2004006) for Roma and Sinti.
1.1.4.2.3.4.3. Pro: Respect for the rights of persons belonging to minorities is one of the values of the EU. This value is explicitly mentioned in Art 2 of the [Treaty on EU](http://eur-lex.europa.eu/LexUriServ/LexUriServ.do?uri=OJ:C:2008:115:0013:0045:en:PDF).
1.1.4.2.3.5. Con: The [millet system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgarian_Millet) of the Ottoman allowed for the aquisition of independent political power on the Balkan. Minority rights on the Balkan in 1990 helped little in contrast.
1.1.4.2.3.5.1. Pro: It was in the early 1990s that Yugoslavia disintegrated because of failed minority protection; e.g. through the [Ten-Day War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ten-Day_War) and the [Croatian War of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Croatian_War_of_Independence).
1.1.4.2.3.5.2. Pro: 1989 saw ethnical cleansing of minorities in Bulgaria against the [Turkish minority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgarian_Turks#The_.22Big_Excursion.22).
1.1.4.2.4. Pro: Getting divorced or bringing up a child as a single parent was easier in the 1990s.

1.1.4.2.4.4. Con: A child was more expensive in the 1990s than in the 1890s, which makes it more difficult despite a liberalized legal framework.
1.1.4.2.4.4.1. Pro: [The costs](http://www.businessinsider.com/the-surging-cost-of-raising-a-kid-in-two-charts-2012-6?IR=T) of raising a child grew between 1960 and 2010. From this we can infere that raising a child in 1890 was cheaper than in 1990.
1.1.4.2.4.4.2. Pro: [The cost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cost_of_raising_a_child) of raising a child in less developed countries is lower. Because in 1890 Europe was less developed the cost to raise a child were lower.
1.1.4.2.5. Con: Men remained more [informed](http://ec.europa.eu/public_opinion/archives/eb/eb48/eb48_en.pdf) about EU politics than women. This was a significant hurdle for equal participation in the 1990s.
1.1.4.2.6. Con: Men loose their powerful position in an equal society that give women more rights.
1.1.4.2.6.1. Con: Men are still in power.
1.1.4.2.6.1.1. Pro: Across the EU women are [underrepresented](http://ec.europa.eu/justice/gender-equality/gender-decision-making/index_en.htm) in decision-making positions.
1.1.4.2.6.1.2. Pro: There are less female than male [board members](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_representation_on_corporate_boards_of_directors) in big companies.
1.1.4.2.6.1.3. Pro: Men are overrepresented in media and can therefore influence the public opinion.
1.1.4.2.6.1.3.1. Pro: Even though the number of women in media professions, such as journalism, is growing, the media is still statistically [dominated by men](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_and_gender#Careers), who hold the vast majority of power positions.
1.1.4.2.6.1.3.2. Pro: Men are [more likely](http://www.womensmediacenter.com/pages/the-problem) to be quoted than women in the media, and more likely to cover "serious" topics.

1.1.4.2.6.2.1. Pro: Many men enjoy spending more time with their children.
1.1.4.2.6.2.2. Pro: Less work means more time for leisure activities.
1.1.4.2.6.2.3. Con: With increased [double burden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Double_burden) for women, men can reduce their family obligations without reducing their position of power.

1.1.4.2.7.1. Pro: In the 1890s, [homosexuality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homosexuality#Europe) was treated as 'abnormal' triggering Havelock Ellis to challenge these theories.

1.1.4.3. Con: There are still many [monarchies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monarchies_in_Europe#/media/File:European_monarchies.svg) in Europe and they enrich the life of European citizens.
1.1.4.3.1. Pro: Media and entertainment profit from monarchies.
1.1.4.3.1.1. Pro: A royal wedding or birth of a new prince or princess guarantees high runs of magazines or online click numbers.
1.1.4.3.1.2. Con: Merely being an object of mass entertainment and gossip, keeping monarchies running is simply too expensive.
1.1.4.3.1.2.1. Pro: The [British monarchy](http://www.royal.gov.uk/TheRoyalHousehold/Royalfinances/HeadofStateexpenditure.aspx) cost £87.3 million in 1991-92.

1.1.4.4. Con: Most European monarchies were not absolute in the 1890s anymore.

1.1.6. Pro: Legal protection made life more comfortable by reducing hazardous and uncomfortable situations.
1.1.6.1. Pro: The conditions for [prisoners](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=bwvH5ce94eIC&pg=PA196&lpg=PA196&dq=prison+system+1900+europe&source=bl&ots=UdkT5glLxS&sig=snY1e9NTafJLFP1l04sNt-zWUOk&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjFip3_lefKAhXB6KYKHTw0Dr0Q6AEISzAJ#v=onepage&q&f=false) improved significantly. This allows marginalized groups to enjoy a better quality of life.
1.1.6.1.1. Pro: Countries like Great Britain or France do not send criminals to penal colonies anymore.

1.1.6.1.4. Pro: Capital punishment had been abolished in Europe by the 1990s.
1.1.6.1.5. Pro: The United Nations Convention against Torture and Other Cruel, Inhuman or Degrading Treatment or Punishment is in force since 1987.
1.1.6.2. Pro: Working conditions have improved a lot.
1.1.6.2.1. Pro: Laws on child labour have increased childrens' rights.

1.1.6.2.3. Pro: Laws on working hours improved the workers' lives.
1.1.6.2.4. Pro: Laws regarding security on the workplace made working safer for everyone.

1.1.6.2.4.2. Con: Migrant workers often face discrimination and are exposed to more dangers on the job.
1.1.6.3. Pro: Products became much safer for consumers because authorities put in place protective measures.
1.1.6.3.1. Pro: [Toy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toy_safety#European_regulations) safety standards are in place protecting the most vulnerable in society.
1.1.6.3.2. Pro: Food safety standards were meagre in the 1890s.
1.1.6.3.2.1. Pro: It was not until after World War II that consumer interest in and need for nutrition information became [evident](http://pkt.jinakarn.com/ept.pdf).
1.1.6.3.2.1.1. Pro: The first institute that dealt with Food Safety was the 1961 established [Monde Selection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monde_Selection).
1.1.6.3.2.1.2. Pro: It was not before the [1950s](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=4chKCAAAQBAJ&pg=PA6&lpg=PA6&dq=Sale+of+Food+and+Drugs+Act+1875&source=bl&ots=ml8ViULgCl&sig=Ey-9_69jkZFQsHStbTzK5bROvZE&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwiIsKLEsurKAhVFn5QKHaaACDkQ6AEIOzAF#v=onepage&q&f=false) food laws took [consumer](http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/780408) protection into account.
1.1.6.3.2.1.3. Pro: Science was not well aware of the [relation](http://www.food-safety-and-you.com/HistoryofFoodSafety.html) between spoiled food and illness by 1890.
1.1.6.3.2.2. Con: The [meat](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=ZhIJP-40hkgC&pg=PR11&lpg=PR11&dq=food+safety+19th+century&source=bl&ots=rJWLCFXRMO&sig=Hw02j3HbBBebV1K7NBVyqSNb7AM&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjhraK6serKAhWIlJQKHecLBUoQ6AEIKDAC#v=onepage&q&f=false) inspection procedure established in the mid 19th century was essentially the same as in 1990.

1.1.7.3.1.1. Pro: Progress and advances in the health sector had a positive impact on the quality of life in the 1990s.

1.1.7.3.1.1.1.1. Pro: Because costs of medical services are low and do not have to be carried alone by the patient and in general better medical treatments were developed to treat all kinds of medical problems, the body is exposed to threats such as alcohol, smoking, unhealthy diets, etc., which to a huge amount depend on the habits of the consumer.

1.1.7.3.1.1.3.1. Pro: There were many jobs in the 1990s, in which people had to sit for many hours in front of their desktops. This kind of work has [negative consequences](http://www.makeuseof.com/tag/5-reasons-working-with-computers-is-bad-for-you-how-to-stay-healthy/) on people's health like notable weight gaining, diabetes, heart diseases and back pain,etc.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.1.1. Con: In the 1890s the majority had to do manual labor under poor conditions in factories or on fields. This kind of work had negative consequences for the human body as well.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.2. Pro: [Obesity](http://www.euro.who.int/en/health-topics/noncommunicable-diseases/obesity) amongst European citizens has become a major health issue.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.2.1. Pro: Obesity costs Europe [€81 billion](http://www.env-health.org/IMG/pdf/obesity_diabetes.pdf) per year while the eradication of [smallpox](http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10681974) cost only $300 million. That makes obesity a much graver problem.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.2.1.1. Con: Health issues are not only about money. Of all those infected, 20–60 percent—and over 80 percent of infected children—[died](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC1200696/) from smallpox.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.2.1.1.1. Con: Obesity is directly linked with [mortality](https://www.noo.org.uk/NOO_about_obesity/mortality). It is thus also not only about money.

1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.5.2.4.11. Pro: In order to achieve "tasty artificially engineered food" flavor enhancers like monosodium glutamate \(MSG\) are used extensively. Headache, flushing, numbness, nausea, rapid flattering heartbeats and some other symptoms after consuming MSG are summarized as the MSG [symptom complex](http://www.mayoclinic.org/healthy-lifestyle/nutrition-and-healthy-eating/expert-answers/monosodium-glutamate/faq-20058196).
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.5.2.4.11.1. Con: Usually the MSG symptoms are [mild](http://www.mayoclinic.org/healthy-lifestyle/nutrition-and-healthy-eating/expert-answers/monosodium-glutamate/faq-20058196) and no medical treatment is needed.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.5.2.4.11.2. Con: Researchers have not found any concrete [evidences](http://www.mayoclinic.org/healthy-lifestyle/nutrition-and-healthy-eating/expert-answers/monosodium-glutamate/faq-20058196) of a connection between the symptom complex and MSG.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.5.2.4.11.3. Con: MSG do not have actual effects and is more a [myth](http://www.businessinsider.com/facts-about-natural-and-artificial-flavors-2014-1).
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.5.2.4.11.4. Pro: A [scientific experiment](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/10644540) has shown that fifteen minutes after ingesting MSG the blood serum insulin increase threefold. It takes more than 100 minutes to get to normal levels again. This happens in abscence of ingesting \(carbohydrate\) glucose. Maybe for some the insulin cascading effect is mild, but for others it could be debilitating.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.5.2.4.11.4.1. Pro: Moments of acute higher serum insulin drives hunger, may lead to eating more \(carbohydrate\) convenience food and snacking. Insulin also drives glucose once changed by the liver into fat into the fat cells of adipose tissue, thus a cause for obesity.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.5.3. Pro: MSGs where invented by [Kikuna Ikeda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kikunae_Ikeda) at the beginning of the 20th century only. Thus, there was little impact in the 19th century.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.5.4. Con: The use of artificial colors and flavors makes food cheaper.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.5.4.1. Pro: It is not necessary to make use of real fruits but instead use their aroma only. Using aroma instead of fruit is cheaper.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.5.4.1.1. Pro: Joghurt is often having aroma with only a slight part of real fruits in it.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.5.4.1.2. Pro: Vanilla sugar does contain mostly vanilla aroma instead of real vanilla. That is why the non-ecological one is so much cheaper.
1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.5.4.2. Con: The only effects of food colors are to make it more attractive. This does not reduce the price.

1.1.7.3.1.1.8.1. Pro: In London [syphilis](http://www.independent.co.uk/life-style/love-sex/culture-of-love/a-brief-cultural-history-of-sex-938527.html) spread wildly between prostitutes, their clients and their clients' families
1.1.7.3.1.1.8.2. Con: The human immunodeficiency virus infection and acquired immune deficiency syndrome [\(HIV/AIDS\)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HIV/AIDS#History) was first clinically observed in 1981.
1.1.7.3.1.1.8.3. Pro: [Child prostitution](https://www.mtholyoke.edu/courses/rschwart/hist255-s01/eponine2/exploitation.html) was widespread in 19th century Paris, as daughters - frequently prepubescent - were forced into sexual encounters with bourgeouis men for as little as a single franc.
1.1.7.3.1.1.9. Pro: Malnutrition [virtually disappeared](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=RLBfzNkGfx8C&printsec=frontcover&dq=A+Social+History+of+Twentieth-+Century+Europe&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwi4ve7W1IzMAhUBX5QKHZkNBMcQ6AEIGzAA) from Europe over the course of the 20th century.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10. Con: In the 1890s there were less widespread human diseases as well as epizootics than in the 1990s.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.1.7.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.1.8.2.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.3. Con: Europe faced several outbreaks of [Cholera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pandemic#Cholera) around 1890.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.3.1. Pro: There were fifteen [Cholera epidemics](https://books.google.co.uk/books?id=wUe4AwAAQBAJ&printsec=frontcover&hl=de&source=gbs_ge_summary_r&cad=0#v=onepage&q&f=false) in Hamburg in the 19th century.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.4. Con: [Smallpox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pandemic) has been completely eradicated.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.5. Con: Typhus [Vaccines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Typhus#20th_century) were developed during the 20th century.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.6. Pro: The [Ebola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ebola_virus_disease) virus disease \(EVD\) was first identified in 1976.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.6.1. Con: Just because the Ebola virus has been identified in 1976 does not obligatorily mean it did not exist before.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.6.1.1. Con: There were no incidents before [1976](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ebola_virus_disease).
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.6.2. Con: There was no Ebola victim in a European country.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.6.3. Pro: This made travelling African countries a lot more unsafe for Europeans.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.7. Pro: Bovine spongiform encephalopathy [\(BSE\)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bovine_spongiform_encephalopathy) only became a big deal in the 1990s.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.7.1. Con: Worldwide only [228](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bovine_spongiform_encephalopathy#Epidemiology) people became infected by BSE. This is only a minor health issue.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.7.1.1. Con: In humans, autopsy tests are not always done, so the figure of 228 human BSE cases is likely to be too low.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.7.1.2. Pro: Until 2000, the British [death](http://www.theguardian.com/uk/2000/sep/05/bse.foodanddrink) toll for BSE stood at only 74 persons.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.8. Con: There is no [Malaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaria#History) in Europe anymore.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.9. Pro: The earliest infections of humans with the Influenza A virus subtype H5N1 occurred in [1997](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_A_virus_subtype_H5N1#Epidemiology).
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.9.1. Con: Nearly all infections occurred in [Southeast Asia](https://www.washingtonpost.com/national/health-science/flu-scientists-agree-to-60-day-pause-in-bird-flu-research/2012/01/20/gIQAzl2TEQ_story.html).
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.9.2. Pro: This made travelling Asian countries a lot more unsafe for Europeans.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.10. Con: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.1.6.8.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.11. Con: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.1.6.9.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.12. Con: The big [pandemics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pandemic) like Cholera, Typhus and Smallpox cost several million Europeans their lives.
1.1.7.3.1.1.10.13. Con: The [1889–1890 flu pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1889%E2%80%9390_flu_pandemic) spread across all of Europe and killed around 1 million. This is more than any pandemic in the 1990s.
1.1.7.3.1.1.11. Con: Improved communication technology increased the stress level, because everyone was available at most times, due to widespread telephone [landlines](http://www.slate.com/articles/business/moneybox/2008/07/phones_without_homes.html) and spreading [cell phones](http://www.knowyourmobile.com/nokia/nokia-3310/19848/history-mobile-phones-1973-2008-handsets-made-it-all-happen).
1.1.7.3.1.1.11.1. Pro: There is a [link](http://www.huffingtonpost.com/david-volpi-md-pc-facs/technology-depression_b_1723625.html) between technology use and fatigue and stress.
1.1.7.3.1.1.11.2. Pro: With modern communication technology there were more chances for [procrastination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Procrastination).
1.1.7.3.1.1.11.2.1. Pro: Watching TV causes the production of [dopamine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_aspects_of_television#Psychological_effects) creating a feeling of satisfaction. This encourages to watch more and procrastinate.
1.1.7.3.1.1.11.2.2. Pro: The advent of PC games allowed to consume a lot of time instead of being productive.
1.1.7.3.1.1.11.2.2.1. Con: Playing video games stimulates important [skills](http://www.creativeteachingsite.com/videogames.htm): Logical thinking, observation skills, careful reading, map making and reading skills, problem solving, developing strategies, etc.
1.1.7.3.1.1.11.2.2.1.1. Pro: The [British](http://kotaku.com/5164562/royal-air-force-prefers-gamers-to-pilots) and the [U.S.](https://gcn.com/blogs/emerging-tech/2013/04/do-video-gamers-make-good-drone-pilots.aspx) air force are even recruiting their drone pilots from game conventions.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12. Pro: The average person's health over his whole lifetime has increased tremendously, due to much improved and accessible healthcare.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.1. Pro: The health situation for disabled people increased tremendously.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.1.1. Pro: In 1980 the World Health Organization \(WHO\) introduced a framework for working with disability, publishing the "International Classification of Impairments, Disabilities and Handicaps".
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.1.2. Pro: The first lightweight [wheelchair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wheelchair#History) was invented in 1933 and made the life of people with disabilities easier.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.1.3. Pro: It was only in the wake of WWII that modern [prosthesis](http://www.amputee-coalition.org/resources/a-brief-history-of-prosthetics/) allowed for a return to normal life for amputees.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.1.3.1. Con: For prosthetic arms, WW I \(not II\) spawned the Carnes Arm, or the Sauerbruch hand  which was popular until the Fifties and provided a fast, finely tuned, direct and propriosensory control and body powered hooks, top for hard work until today. Another post WWI \(not II\) innovation was the Krukenberg arm \(not a prosthesis, functionally extremely relevant\).
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.1.3.2. Pro: A post-WW II innovation was the "Russian Arm" \(myoelectric\) which still is more of a gadget than a rehabilitation tool for real work.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.1.4. Pro: [Autism](http://www.webmd.com/brain/autism/history-of-autism) was just detected in the 20th century. Before, those suffering from it had to endure social exclusion for their unusual behavior.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.1.4.1. Pro: [Treatments](http://www.webmd.com/brain/autism/history-of-autism) to ease autism just emerged in the 1960s and thus made life of people suffering from it much easier.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.1.5. Pro: It was only in the 1980s that the causes of [cerebral palsy](http://www.birthinjuryguide.org/cerebral-palsy/history/) were discovered. This is necessary for identifying proper treatment.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.1.6. Pro: The understanding that the [Down syndrome](http://www.nads.org/about-us/history-of-nads/) is caused by an extra chromosome did not become widespread until the 1960s.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.1.7. Pro: Survival rates of those born with [spina bifida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spina_bifida) was only 10% before the [1960s](http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3408685/). The rates were higher in the [1990s](http://www.webmd.com/children/news/20110210/fetal-surgery-better-odds-for-spina-bifida-kids).
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.1.7.1. Pro: Survival rates of those with spina bifida have improved due to improving medical treatments. One of the most significant was the development of the [shunt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cerebral_shunt), and more recently, the computerized shunt. One of the most common causes of death and severe mental disability in babies with spina bifida \(aside from infection\) is severe hydrocephalus, build up of spinal fluid in the ventricles of the brain.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.2. Pro: The [size](http://www.bbc.com/news/health-23896855) of average European men has increased by 10 centimeters which indicates a healthier society.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.3. Pro: Average [life expectancy](http://ourworldindata.org/data/population-growth-vital-statistics/life-expectancy/) has increased substantially.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.3.1. Pro: The mortality [Gini](http://ourworldindata.org/data/health/health-inequality/) coefficient has reduced significantly until 1990 indicating that health benefits are evenly spread among the population.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.4. Pro: [Child mortality](http://ourworldindata.org/data/population-growth-vital-statistics/child-mortality/) has decreased tremendously since 1890.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.5. Pro: [Infant mortality](http://ourworldindata.org/data/population-growth-vital-statistics/infant-mortality/) has decreased very much since 1890.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.6. Pro: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.1.12.3.1.
1.1.7.3.1.1.12.7. Pro: [Maternal mortality](http://ourworldindata.org/data/health/maternal-mortality/) decreased drastically since 1890.
1.1.7.3.1.2. Pro: Educational opportunities for average Europeans were much better in the 1990s.
1.1.7.3.1.2.1. Pro: [Tertiary education](http://science.jrank.org/pages/9080/Education-in-Europe-Nineteenth-Twentieth-Century-Education.html) has broadened beyond the privileged between 1890 and 1990.
1.1.7.3.1.2.1.1. Pro: Only at the end of the 19th century were women allowed to enroll in universities, and only over the course of the 20th century did the share of women enrolled start to equal that of men.
1.1.7.3.1.2.2. Pro: [Reforms](http://publications.jrc.ec.europa.eu/repository/bitstream/JRC57357/reqno_jrc57357.pdf) of the education sector have made it inclusive and more specialized.
1.1.7.3.1.2.3. Pro: [International mobility](https://www.utwente.nl/bms/cheps/summer_school/literature/internationalisation.pdf) of students has increased after World War II after Council of Europe initiatives.
1.1.7.3.1.2.4. Con: Mass education makes upward social mobility more difficult.
1.1.7.3.1.2.4.1. Pro: White collar workers become increasingly [proletarianized](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=ByAi5XQiz9cC&pg=PA179&lpg=PA179&dq=proletarianization+of+white+collar+workers&source=bl&ots=1rfeCzDkof&sig=ZV7QeBT-oCY8M_xv7akrcDv7tJc&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwiwzdWJkOrKAhVFVZQKHcmMCXIQ6AEINDAF#v=onepage&q&f=false) because of their abundance in the labor market.
1.1.7.3.1.2.4.2. Con: A college degree is a [ticket out of poverty](http://www.brookings.edu/research/reports/2013/06/13-facts-higher-education).
1.1.7.3.1.2.4.3. Con: Investment in education yields very [high returns](http://www.brookings.edu/research/reports/2013/06/13-facts-higher-education).
1.1.7.3.1.2.4.4. Pro: A degree alone will not hire you anymore. With increasing mass education, other factors, such as additional language skills, experience abroad, or connections become more important.
1.1.7.3.1.2.4.4.1. Con: Higher educational attainment correlates with [lower](https://www.oecd.org/edu/ceri/38038265.pdf) unemployment rates, and only a [minority](http://link.springer.com/article/10.1023%2FA%3A1016357826723) of graduates faced problems on the job market during the 1990s. A degree therefore hires you more likely than no degree.
1.1.7.3.1.2.4.5. Pro: If everybody achieves relatively high degrees \(in this example an equivalent to the Abitur, means the right to visit an university\) jobs, which do not need those educational ranks are getting more and more unattractive.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5. Con: Since the 1890s there has been a decrease in broad and profound education in culture, languages and literature.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.1. Con: Schools in the 1890s were teaching propaganda to create soldiers and a nation.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.1.1. Pro: In Italy, the [schools](http://science.jrank.org/pages/9080/Education-in-Europe-Nineteenth-Twentieth-Century-Education.html) made a national hero out of the heroic fighting [Giuseppe Garibaldi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi).
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.1.2. Pro: Governments believed that the [primary purpose](http://science.jrank.org/pages/9080/Education-in-Europe-Nineteenth-Twentieth-Century-Education.html) of universal elementary schooling was to raise honest, hardworking, useful citizens.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.1.3. Pro: Classical subjects like Latin or history are very powerful to create an image of historical continuity and therewith unify citizens.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.2. Pro: [In France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_education#France), classical education had made way for more science oriented teaching by the late18th century.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.3. Pro: "[Humanistische Bildung](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humanistisches_Gymnasium#Vor_dem_Zweiten_Weltkrieg)" played a less and less important role in education, especially in Germany, but also in other European countries.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.4. Pro: Remnants of this form of education have been transferred to an university level, as apparent in the English "[Humanities](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Studia_humanitatis)".
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.5. Con: [In the Netherlands](https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gymnasium) they seperated science and culture oriented high schools already in 1876.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.6. Con: By the 1990s English had become a major part of all curricula.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.7. Con: In the 1990s, the [Liceo Classico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liceo_classico) system was still in place in Italy and most academics were educated in these.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.8. Con: In most European countries a school system that included [classical education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gymnasium_%28school%29#Germany), such as Latin, was still in place.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.9. Con: In the 1990s, more people had the chance to study in advanced schools that educate culture, language, and literature.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.9.1. Pro: [Educational reforms](http://science.jrank.org/pages/9080/Education-in-Europe-Nineteenth-Twentieth-Century-Education.html) in the 1960s and 1990s aimed at making secondary education more inclusive.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.10. Pro: The classical curriculum benefited the student regardless of his or her future career because it developed the individual.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.11. Con: The 1990s offered a bigger variety of established schooling forms.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.11.1. Pro: Even though [Montessori schools](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Montessori_education) were developed in the late 19th century, the first class opened after the 1890s.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.11.2. Pro: [Waldorf Schools](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waldorf_education#Origins_and_history) became widespread only in the second half of the 20th century.
1.1.7.3.1.2.5.11.3. Pro: The [Regio Emilia approach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reggio_Emilia_approach) was just developed in the second half of the 20th century.
1.1.7.3.1.2.6. Pro: [Literacy rates](http://ourworldindata.org/data/education-knowledge/literacy/) increased dramatically since 1900.
1.1.7.3.1.3. Pro: The economic situation had improved significantly for the majority of the population.
1.1.7.3.1.3.1. Pro: The housing situation has improved for Europeans until 1990.
1.1.7.3.1.3.1.1. Con: Housing [prices](http://observationsandnotes.blogspot.kr/2011/06/us-housing-prices-since-1900.html) have soared since 1900.
1.1.7.3.1.3.1.2. Pro: Most houses had a toilet, heater and a bathroom with warm water in the 1990s while this was not the case in 1890.
1.1.7.3.1.3.1.3. Pro: At the turn of the century the housing situation for the poor was ['problematic'](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=iAIs0MI-xgsC&pg=PA98&lpg=PA98&dq=housing+situation+1890+europe&source=bl&ots=J5m52Vqw31&sig=uyu9OIZzka0RYyrQ41MhEZDeqXw&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjJzLCugOrKAhXG26YKHWH9CNs4ChDoAQggMAE#v=onepage&q&f=false) across Europe.
1.1.7.3.1.3.1.3.1. Pro: In 1880s, the Housing act in [Ireland](http://www.irishstatutebook.ie/eli/1890/act/70/enacted/en/print) and the [UK](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Housing_of_the_Working_Classes_Act_1885) recognized poor conditions of the working class. This is representative of Europe as a whole.
1.1.7.3.1.3.1.4. Pro: The gap in housing conditions between the poor and the rich has narrowed.
1.1.7.3.1.3.1.4.1. Pro: Social housing across Europe helped to raise the minimum housing standard.
1.1.7.3.1.3.1.4.1.1. Pro: [Vienna](http://www.shareable.net/blog/public-housing-works-lessons-from-vienna-and-singapore) started widespread social housing projects in the early 20th century and was able to  the general housing condition for workers.
1.1.7.3.1.3.1.4.1.2. Pro: In 1903, [Italy](http://www.housingeurope.eu/resource-111/social-housing-in-europe) started a social housing project that helped the poor to raise their housing standard.
1.1.7.3.1.3.1.4.1.3. Pro: In the [UK](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_housing_in_the_United_Kingdom#History), before 1890 the state was not involved in social housing but then replaced slums with social housing.
1.1.7.3.1.3.1.4.1.4. Pro: In [socialist regimes](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/24080762_Social_housing_in_the_Czech_Republic_Poland_and_Slovakia), social housing was provided by the government helping to rebuild the housing destroyed in World War II from which citizens are still profiting.
1.1.7.3.1.3.1.5. Con: Until 1990 rents [rose](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=s_WFhNrMc1gC&pg=PA50&lpg=PA50&dq=munich+rent+1990&source=bl&ots=QsmLYlsoWe&sig=z9a9Pa7q5Q1nc1ITBOTml9K-zLc&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjcoKX6iurKAhUBMZQKHRy-AwMQ6AEIJzAB#v=onepage&q=munich%20rent%201990&f=false) in the Western part of Europe making it more difficult to find decent housing conditions.
1.1.7.3.1.3.2. Pro: After significant declines throughout the past century, virtually [no absolute poverty](http://www.cgdev.org/blog/poverty-rich-world-when-it-was-not-nearly-so-rich) exists in Europe anymore.
1.1.7.3.1.3.2.1. Con: While above the standards of developing countries, [up to 6%](http://www.euro.centre.org/data/1226583242_93408.pdf) of the population in Europe's poorest countries live under the absolute poverty rate of 5€/day, and [up to 50%](http://feantsaresearch.all2all.org/IMG/pdf/policy-review-5.pdf) suffer from some form of deprivation.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3. Pro: [Globalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Globalization) allowed for much better trade and capital movement.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.1. Con: Globalization took jobs in many industries - for example [textile, clothing and footwear](http://www.ilo.org/global/about-the-ilo/newsroom/news/WCMS_008075/lang--en/index.htm) - from European countries to developing countries.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.2. Con: Globalization makes countries [vulnerable](http://siteresources.worldbank.org/DEC/Resources/32459_Schmukler,_Zoido,_and_Halac_\(Oct2003\).pdf) to international economic crises and financial contagion.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.2.1. Con: There were no Europe wide financial crises in the 1990s.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.2.2. Con: Financial crisis existed before globalization, e.g. in the [late 13th century](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/finance/4128072/England-suffered-a-financial-crisis-in-the-Middle-Ages.html).
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.3. Con: Globalization goes hand in hand with the [emergence of tax havens](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=2KZQabqIOkoC&pg=PR4&dq=Tax+Havens:+How+Globalization+Really+Works&hl=en&sa=X&redir_esc=y#v=onepage&q&f=false) that allow companies and rich individuals to evade regulation, skew the benefits of globalization and precipitate financial crises.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.4. Con: Transnational criminals, smugglers and traffickers have been among the [major beneficiaries](http://www.cfr.org/transnational-crime/globalization-affects-transnational-crime/p28403) of globalization. It makes regulation and law enforcement more difficult, and provides new avenues for evasion and illicit cooperation.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.5. Con: Globalization undermines states' [tax autonomy](http://pas.sagepub.com/content/30/2/245) and their ability to effectively impose [taxes on mobile factors](http://www.e-jei.org/upload/JEI_20_3_530_542_524.pdf) such as capital.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.6. Pro: Globalization provides consumers with a [greater variety of goods](https://www.nber.org/papers/w10314) to choose from.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.6.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.8.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.7. Pro: Integration of financial markets and trade helps foster peace.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.7.1. Pro: Parts of society that are interested in trade will demand that trade flows remain stable and not be disrupted by conflict.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.7.2. Pro: The GATT/WTO system builds confidence and trust among members by providing a legal framework.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.7.3. Pro: Market protection contributed to the outbreak of the Pacific War in 1941.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.7.3.1. Con: There were other factors, like a Japanese identity crisis or dominance of military men, that made them attack Pearl Harbor.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.7.4. Con: Countries fight, even if their economies are deeply integrated, such as in WWI.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.8. Pro: Globalization proceeds according to rules which are easier to live with than with a system based on power.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.9. Pro: Freer trade cuts the cost of living by reducing prices.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.9.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.1.1.2.2.2.
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.10. Pro: Freer trade raises income, such as those facilitated by the [Uruguay Round](http://www.ub.edu/prometheus21/articulos/archivos/gatt.PDF).
1.1.7.3.1.3.3.11. Pro: Free trade stimulates economic [growth](http://europa.eu/pol/pdf/flipbook/en/trade_en.pdf).
1.1.7.3.1.3.4. Pro: An organized system of state welfare provision \(social security\) was not common back in the 1890s, but it was in the 1990's.
1.1.7.3.1.3.4.1. Pro: Since 1948, [social security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_security#History) is a concept enshrined in Article 22 of the Universal Declaration of Human Rights.
1.1.7.3.1.3.5. Pro: With the abolishment of aristocracy income inequalities were reduced in Europe between the1890s and the 1990s.
1.1.7.3.1.3.5.1. Pro: In [Denmark](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=57nvtVnTUzIC&pg=PA223&lpg=PA223&dq=gini+coefficient+europe+1900&source=bl&ots=NfpkUG2Ipz&sig=ratxgViUEl5F3T1St110cUfVl3A&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjjjfrcmITNAhUDJZQKHWxABpwQ6AEIODAI#v=onepage&q&f=false) the Gini coefficient reduced from .50 at the end of the 19th century to .27 in 1963.
1.1.7.3.1.3.5.2. Pro: The [top 1%](https://ourworldindata.org/income-inequality/) share of total income reduced dramatically between 1900 and the 1990s. This indicates that income inequality reduced.
1.1.7.3.1.3.5.3. Pro: The Gini coefficient reduced in the [UK](https://ourworldindata.org/income-inequality/) between 1890s and 1990s.
1.1.7.3.1.3.6. Con: Unemployment rates in major European countries such as the UK, Germany and France were [at least twice higher](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=ssNMAgAAQBAJ&pg=RA4-PA148&lpg=RA4-PA148&dq=unemployment+rates+1890+europe&source=bl&ots=5Tmi-U8bWZ&sig=B6VSQvBhGPWOICdVYB1VUJdCNbs&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwiJ08L5j5_NAhVKF5QKHWaWBxsQ6AEINTAD#v=onepage&q=unemployment%20rates%201890%20europe&f=false) in 1990 than in 1890. The percentage of the population living on a self-earned income thus decreased.
1.1.7.3.1.3.6.1. Con: Even if unemployed the [disposable income](http://www.roiw.org/1989/1.pdf) increased for families and therewith strengthened their financial independence.
1.1.7.3.1.4. Pro: The society in the 1990s was more considerate and civilized than in the 1890s and thus better to live in. Citizens enjoyed better legal protection, were nicer towards each other and were taken care of in case of need.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1. Con: In the 1990s mass produced goods were a standard in most European countries, which led to a reckless consumer society that is inhumane towards others.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.1. Pro: Europeans owned more things in the 1990s than in the 1890s.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.2. Con: A reckless society in the 1990s that is exploiting the earth's resources is no harm to Europeans as long as the damages are felt abroad.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.2.1. Con: Damages abroad are going to affect Europeans eventually. Those who suffer the damages will start to emigrate sooner or later - many of them facing Europe.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.2.1.1. Pro: Since the 1990s, Antarctic total column ozone in September and October continued to be 40–50% lower than pre-ozone-hole values \([ozone depletion](http://acdb-ext.gsfc.nasa.gov/Documents/O3_Assessments/Docs/WMO_2010/Q2_QA.pdf)\).
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.2.1.2. Con: There is no [academic](http://www.migrationpolicy.org/pubs/MPIEurope-EnvironmentalMigration.pdf) consensus on the causalities between environmental degradation and migration to Europe. Especially, most modern academics doubt the early findings.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.2.1.3. Con: Europeans in the 1990s did not suffer from the fact that their consumption hurt the environment or other people.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.3. Con: A consumer society is benefitial for Europeans.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.3.1. Pro: There is a great amount of choice to select from for every product.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.3.2. Pro: Stores specialize and therewith reflect buyer preferences.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.3.2.1. Con: Stores were specialized before.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.3.2.2. Con: Lots of goods before the introduction of massproduction were custom made \(e.g. fashion and furniture\).
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.3.2.2.1. Con: Further specialization within sectors is good for the economy because people can buy higher quality products in stores that specialize according to their [comparative advantage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comparative_advantage).
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.3.3. Pro: The consumer society creates competition and therewith innovation.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.3.4. Pro: A consumer society helps to grow economically without relying on exports alone.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.3.5. Pro: Consumer research emerged as a new field of emplyoment.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.3.6. Pro: Many companies make much money by providing consumer goods.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.4. Con: Consumerism [emerged](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consumerism#Origins) already in the late 19th century.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.5. Con: The emergence of a consumer society leveled social hierarchies and made everybody more equal. Thus, consumerism is a grand quest for creating an equal society.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.5.1. Pro: Goods become available for the masses and not only for a selected few.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.5.1.1. Pro: It is very easy to get a credit card \(for example the [Amazon credit card](http://www.amazon.com/Credit-Cards/b?node=1266766011)\) or credit financing \(for example [Apple](http://www.apple.com/uk/shop/browse/finance/PaypalFinancingLandingPage)\). Huge retail companies even advertise it.

1.1.7.3.1.4.1.5.3.1. Pro: Not everyone can buy very expensive brands and thus need to remain behind in their conspicuous consumption.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.5.3.2. Con: Conspicuous consumption has existed [before](http://www.emeraldinsight.com/doi/abs/10.1108/10610420810856495) the advent of a consumer society.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.5.4. Con: Purchase of certain goods allows people to identify like-minded individuals through the display of similar products. This furthers social stratification.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.5.4.1. Con: Professions and social groups had characteristic clothing and items before. Thus, social stratification is no result of consumerism.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.6. Con: If consumerism would be that negative for Europeans then they would simply stop it. Apparently it is not that negative.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.6.1. Pro: In some cases [shopping](http://www.madisonindia.com/media/pdf/WhyPeopleShop.pdf) helps to bust stress or has a recreational effect.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.6.2. Pro: People simply [enjoy](http://qz.com/640729/americans-basically-agree-that-shopping-is-a-great-cure-for-boredom/) shopping.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.6.3. Con: People do a lot of things that are negative for them though they know of the negative consequences.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.6.3.1. Pro: People smoke, drink alcohol, do drugs and eat unhealthy though they know it is bad for their health.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.6.3.2. Con: Behavior with negative consequences is based on rational pro/con analysis. Just that the short term benefits are weighed more heavily. This is even stronger with consumerism where the long term benefits are minimal to the individual.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.6.4. Con: Europeans also simply suppress big food scandals within weeks and keep consuming the same products, because the prices are more important to them than their own health and the environment. Still this is negative to Europeans.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.6.4.1. Con: Food scandals are the exception.

1.1.7.3.1.4.1.7.1.1. Pro: While eating their normal source of food, plastic ingestion can be unavoidable to wildlife. Thus, many of the fish & seafood Europeans consumed were contaminated.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.7.2. Pro: [Acid rain](https://educnet.enpc.fr/pluginfile.php/5882/mod_resource/content/0/Menz-ESP-2004.pdf) increased in Europe and caused local concerns from the 1970s onwards.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8. Pro: In the 1990s it was possible to produce luxury goods in an industrial fashion, which led to an increasing amount of pretentiousness amongst Europeans.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.1. Con: A widespread feeling of decadence and pretentiousness was observable in late 19th century Europe with the emergence of the [decadent movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decadent_movement).
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.1.1. Con: The Decadent movement was a late 19th-century artistic and literary movement of Western Europe and not connected to consumerism.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.2. Pro: In the 1990s luxury products, such as expensive cars, were mass productions, which led to the suggestion that many more people could afford such a product compared to the 1890s.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.2.1. Con: Most of those "luxury products" did not exist back in the 1890s to begin with.

1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.2.2.1.1. Pro: More widespread luxury goods are representing a more equal society rather than decadence and pretentiousness.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.2.2.1.1.1. Pro: Originally the term [conspicuous consumption](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conspicuous_consumption) only applied to the upper class, but now it was extended to society as a whole indicating that classes become blurred.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3. Con: Luxury goods are not a sign of pretentiousness.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.1. Pro: Luxury goods are often the cheapest alternative in the long run.

1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.2. Pro: It is less decadent and pretentious to buy few upscale fashion items than tons of cheap clothing.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3. Con: As economically considered "luxury goods" are a contrast to "necessity goods", they are a sign of pretentiousness.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.1. Con: Cheap clothing is not a necessity good either.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.2. Pro: Necessity goods are goods that we cannot live without and will not likely cut back on even when times are tough, for example food, power, water and gas.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3. Con: People in the 1890s bought lots of things that were no necessity goods too, eg clothing, coffee, chocolate or furniture. Therefore they were not less decadent than people in the 1990s.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3.1. Pro: Since the Napoleonic Wars [coffee](http://eprints.lse.ac.uk/22489/1/wp04.pdf) was consumed by urban workers and rural residents.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3.1.1. Con: [Coffee](http://eprints.lse.ac.uk/22489/1/wp04.pdf) became a necessary \(and widespread\) good in the late 19th century to cope with the regimented time of urban industrialized societies.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3.2. Pro: [Global coffee consumption](http://eprints.lse.ac.uk/22489/1/wp04.pdf) grew more than 15-fold in the 19th century.

1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3.5. Con: Europeans in 1890 consumed much less coffee than those in 1990.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3.5.1. Pro: [Coffee imports](https://research.stlouisfed.org/fred2/series/M07038USM149NNBR) into the US increased drastically since the 1890s. The same trend can be expected for Europe given their parallel economic development and technological progress.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3.5.1.1. Pro: European and US coffee [imports](http://www.web-books.com/Classics/ON/B0/B701/27MB701.html) increased by 2.000.000 bags between 1890 and 1900.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3.5.2. Pro: Coffee was rather expensive in the 1890s while it was affordable in the 1990s. This should have increased the consumption.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3.5.2.1. Pro: In the 1880s, there was a major [disease on Java](http://eprints.lse.ac.uk/22489/1/wp04.pdf) reducing the output of coffee leading to a rise in prices.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3.5.2.2. Pro: The [abolition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abolition_of_slavery_timeline#1850.E2.80.931899) of slavery in the 19th century led to a sudden increase in labor costs that made coffee beans more expensive.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3.5.2.3. Con: New exporters joined the global market decreasing prices.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3.5.2.3.1. Pro: Brazil's [coffee exports](http://eprints.lse.ac.uk/22489/1/wp04.pdf) jumped 75 fold between independence in 1822 and 1899.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3.5.2.3.2. Con: The new capacities were easily matched by the new [market](http://eprints.lse.ac.uk/22489/1/wp04.pdf), the US.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.3.5.3. Pro: The global coffee [production](http://www.ico.org/news/icc-111-5-r1e-world-coffee-outlook.pdf) doubled between the 1960s and 1990s. Thus we can estimate that the amount of possibly consumed coffee in the 1890s was smaller.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.4. Con: Not all luxury goods are signs of pretentiousness because they work as cultural assets.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.4.1. Pro: Music instruments, such as pianos, are not necessary but are a distinct feature of culture.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.4.2. Pro: Pieces of art \(expensive paintings, sculptures etc.\) may not be necessary, but they can be regarded as cultural assets.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.3.5. Pro: Luxury goods are not necessary to survival and thus increase unnecessary costs on someone else. This is decadent.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.4. Con: Luxury goods, such as expensive wines, jewelry, fashion-designer handbags, and luxury cars, are in demand because of the high prices asked for them. The high price makes the goods desirable as symbols of the buyer's high social status, by way of conspicuous consumption and conspicuous leisure. This is a sign of pretentiousness.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.4.1. Pro: Thorstein Veblen was the first economist who identified conspicuous consumption as a mode of status-seeking and identified specific overpriced goods as [Veblen goods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veblen_good).
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.4.1.1. Pro: A perfect example of a Veblen good is the iOS application ["I am rich"](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I_Am_Rich) which is considered to be nothing but decadent having it.
