1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.4.3.4.1.1. Pro: Garment workers start at an early age with training on the job, e.g. with [10 years](http://www.waronwant.org/media/sweatshop-worker-tells-her-story). This makes them highly skilled in their task.

Support personnel measure the [quality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quality_%28business%29) in the degree that a product is reliable, maintainable, or sustainable. Child labour does not fit the criteria.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.4.3.4.1.1.1.2.1. Con: Mainly consumers are concerned with performance, features, reliability, conformance, durability, serviceability, aesthetics and safety when [assessing](http://www.prenhall.com/divisions/bp/app/russellcd/PROTECT/CHAPTERS/CHAP03/HEAD01.HTM) the quality of a product. The quality of production is only marginal for this assessment.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.3.4.3.4.1.1.1.2.1.1. Con: Satisfaction of high-end consumers' concerns and standards is of concern to the producers of high quality products. Thus the quality of production does play a role.

1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.2. Pro: There even is a term for the rise of textile waste referring to the most notorious clothing retailer: the [Primark effect](http://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-1089094/The-Primark-effect-Throwaway-fashion-recycled-makes-30-cent-waste-council-tips.html).
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.3. Pro: The number of clothing items bought per person per year rises constantly.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.3.1. Pro: Fashion became more globalised - and therefore cheaper - in the late 1990s.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.3.1.1. Con: [Fashion](http://www.statista.com/statistics/275318/womens-clothing-prices-cities/) [prices](http://www.statista.com/statistics/275331/mens-clothing-prices-cities/) and expenditure varies greatly with location indicating that globalization has only a minor effect on final prices.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.3.1.2. Pro: Because of falling prices retailers who did not yet produce overseas decided to work with factories in [countries](https://books.google.de/books?id=ETXhAQAAQBAJ&pg=PA14&lpg=PA14&dq=fashion+prices+1990s&source=bl&ots=wXv4YuWhqR&sig=EJiUg6FXB52jjGm2gI8JYue-siw&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjIvePzjv_KAhVFGZoKHZpdAVIQ6AEIZTAL#v=onepage&q=fashion%20prices%201990s&f=false) with lower production costs.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.3.1.3. Pro: The EU lost significant market share of [clothing exports](https://books.google.de/books?id=ETXhAQAAQBAJ&pg=PA14&lpg=PA14&dq=fashion+prices+1990s&source=bl&ots=wXv4YuWhqR&sig=EJiUg6FXB52jjGm2gI8JYue-siw&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjIvePzjv_KAhVFGZoKHZpdAVIQ6AEIZTAL#v=onepage&q=fashion%20prices%201990s&f=false).
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.3.1.4. Pro: A pair of shoes became [36% cheaper](https://books.google.de/books?id=ETXhAQAAQBAJ&pg=PA14&lpg=PA14&dq=fashion+prices+1990s&source=bl&ots=wXv4YuWhqR&sig=EJiUg6FXB52jjGm2gI8JYue-siw&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjIvePzjv_KAhVFGZoKHZpdAVIQ6AEIZTAL#v=onepage&q=fashion%20prices%201990s&f=false) between 1988 and 2004.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.3.1.5. Pro: After the formation of the EU in 1990 the market became quickly integrated and allowed for fiercer competition among producers.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.3.1.5.1. Pro: Zara was able to supply quickly from Spain to Britain when it [expanded](https://books.google.de/books?id=ETXhAQAAQBAJ&pg=PA14&lpg=PA14&dq=fashion+prices+1990s&source=bl&ots=wXv4YuWhqR&sig=EJiUg6FXB52jjGm2gI8JYue-siw&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjIvePzjv_KAhVFGZoKHZpdAVIQ6AEIZTAL#v=onepage&q=fashion%20prices%201990s&f=false) there in the late 1990s.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.3.2. Pro: People increasingly realize, that they can express themselves through what they wear, because that "privilege" is not limited anymore to those who can afford it.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.3.3. Pro: One goal of having "a sneaker for each day of the year" is a pretty often heard "goal/achievement" in Sneakerhead circles.
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.3.4. Pro: In 1997, the average woman in the UK bought 19 items of clothing per year, by 2007 that number was up to 34. \([faircompanies.com](http://faircompanies.com/news/view/fashion-guide-i-slow-fashion/)\)
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.4. Pro: These products are bought just to be thrown away a short while later.

1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.4.2. Pro: Cheap retailer clothings are often of bad quality \(loosening of seems, shrinking after laundry, fading colours, etc.\).
1.1.7.3.1.4.1.8.4.4.3. Pro: Many cheap retailers such as H&M have gone from producing four collections a year \(classic seasons\) to producing multiple collections for every occasion \(even Christmas, NYE, Valentine's Day, etc.\). This encourages consumers to buy more and more.

1.1.7.3.1.4.1.11. Con: In the times of today, the way of how and what we consume became a factor of distinguishing oneself from others, thus consumption being a very advanced form of expressing oneself. This is not reckless.

1.1.7.3.1.4.1.11.2. Pro: [Self-expression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maslow%27s_hierarchy_of_needs) \(Self-actualization\) is the highest need of the individual in societies which focus on the individual, as it is the case in Europe.
1.1.7.3.1.4.2. Pro: At the end of the 19th century [anomie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anomie) was stronger than in the 1990s. Moral obligations were lower and thus reckless behavior was more acceptable.
1.1.7.3.1.4.2.1. Pro: Increased knowledge led to a better understanding of how human behavior contributes to global problems. This knowledge creates a moral obligation to act diligently.
1.1.7.3.1.4.2.2. Pro: In democracies the [anomie level](https://www.soc.umn.edu/~uggen/Zhao_SF_10.pdf) is lower, thus Europeans with successful democratization experience less anomie.
1.1.7.3.1.4.2.3. Con: Marriage is a [crucial determinant](https://www.soc.umn.edu/~uggen/Zhao_SF_10.pdf) of the level of anomie. Reduced rates of wed couples in the 20th century are, thus, increasing the level of anomie.
1.1.7.3.1.4.2.4. Con: Because the [confidence in authorities](https://www.soc.umn.edu/~uggen/Zhao_SF_10.pdf) is lower in the 1990s the level of anomie is higher.
1.1.7.3.1.4.3. Pro: The range of those for whom we [feel empathy](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=J7ATQb6LZX0C&printsec=frontcover&dq=better+angles+of+our+nature&hl=en&sa=X&redir_esc=y#v=onepage&q&f=false) and who we [meet with altruism](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=Yve7lgvtLcsC&printsec=frontcover&dq=expanding+circle&hl=en&sa=X&redir_esc=y#v=onepage&q=expanding%20circle&f=false) has extended beyond the family to nation and race, and ultimately to mankind and society as a whole.
1.1.7.3.1.4.3.1. Con: Hate towards others persist perhaps best seen in [hate crimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hate_crime).
1.1.7.3.1.4.3.2. Con: Altruism is declining in society.
1.1.7.3.1.4.3.2.1. Pro: Measured by [blood](http://www.bmj.com/content/317/7170/1405.1) or [organ](http://www.livescience.com/35844-organ-donation-shortage-study.html) donations, altruism is declining.
1.1.7.3.1.4.3.2.2. Pro: Young people [volunteer](http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1002/nvsm.89/abstract) less often in British society.

Pro: [Voting](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=L41MCgAAQBAJ&pg=PT37&lpg=PT37&dq=decline+in+altruism&source=bl&ots=HIQ1rzDk2Q&sig=-XmTGsHjbm1yZDeMzrVW8VJdjYw&hl=ko&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjXqsiC5JvMAhWSq5QKHZQxB7oQ6AEIQzAE#v=onepage&q&f=false) can be regarded as altruistic act and thus decline in turnout signifies reduced altruism.
1.1.7.3.1.4.3.2.4. Pro: As the population's share living in cities increases, so does altruistic behavior decrease: Stanley Milgram's thesis of ["urban overload"](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=XA8Ho_aITVoC&printsec=frontcover&dq=Crowding+and+Behavior&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwj12IbApprMAhVW2WMKHZepBAoQ6AEIHzAB#v=onepage&q=Crowding%20and%20Behavior&f=false).

Con: Although it is true that welfare took better care of the weak, categories such as "nice", "civilized" and/or "considerate" are so incredibly subjective and culture-specific \(and mind you - Europe is culturally very diverse\), that they simply cannot be used to paint a broad picture of the "quality of life" of the people of the continent.
1.1.7.3.1.5. Pro: The threat of war was less in the 1990s than in the 1890s.

This made people feel safer.

1.1.7.3.1.6. Con: People are happy in the systems they grow up. Even North Koreans think they are [normal](http://www.ncnk.org/resources/publications/Kang%20They%20Think%20Theyre%20Normal.pdf). Thus the likelihood is high that there would not be a change and people of the 1890s would be happy about their times.

Con: During the 1990s, about half the citizens in a number of countries stated [in opinion surveys](https://web.stanford.edu/~ldiamond/papers/howPeopleViewDem.pdf) that democracy is not necessarily always the preferred system of government. 1.1.8. Con: In Victorian England the development of political parties as we know them today was completed by the 1870s.
1.1.8.1. Pro: The '[efficient secret](http://www.cambridge.org/gb/academic/subjects/politics-international-relations/british-government-politics-and-policy/efficient-secret-cabinet-and-development-political-parties-victorian-england)' of UK politics with a Cabinet with not only executive but also legislative predominance developed in the 19th century.

1.3. Con: In the 1990s people were much easier to influence than in 1890s, due to the large reach of media such as the radio or the television.

1.3.6. Con: There were advertisements in the 1890s as well.

1.3.8.6.4.1. Pro: Propaganda wars were fought alongside the [Yugoslavian](http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/europe/591916.stm) Civil War in the 1990s.
1.3.8.6.4.2. Pro: Propaganda was [widespread](http://www.jstor.org/stable/1045133?seq=1#page_scan_tab_contents) on both sides of the Iron Curtain during the Cold War.
1.3.8.6.4.3. Pro: Propaganda was in Western media during the [Rwanda](http://www.globalissues.org/article/405/media-propaganda-and-rwanda) genocide.
1.3.8.7. Con: Propaganda can have positive effects for society.
1.3.8.7.1. Pro: Propaganda was used to campaign for the abolishment of [slavery](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=ABWQVKj00-8C&pg=PA86&redir_esc=y#v=onepage&q&f=false).
1.3.8.7.2. Pro: Pornography of pain was an essential part of developing a [humanitarian](http://www.jstor.org/stable/2169001?seq=1#page_scan_tab_contents) sensibility.
1.3.8.7.3. Pro: Campaigning of societal actors for improvements of living conditions is equally propaganda.
1.3.8.8. Con: Propaganda was existing in [1890](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_propaganda#19th_century) newspapers as well.
1.3.9. Con: In the 1890s newspapers were as widespread as TV and Radio in the 1990s. Thus, they were able to influence the people equally strong.
1.3.9.1. Pro: [Technological](https://chnm.gmu.edu/worldhistorysources/unpacking/newsmod.html) developments led to a strong rise in newspaper circulation.
1.3.9.2. Pro: -> See 1.3.8.6.1.8.2.
1.3.10. Con: -> See 1.3.8.6.1.
1.4. Pro: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.2.
1.5. Pro: Social mobility had increased, thereby enabling people to change their lot and improve their relative social as well as economic standing \(see [here](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=EJeNAgAAQBAJ&pg=PA661&lpg=PA661&dq=social+mobility+since+the+19th+century&source=bl&ots=DPZGKozkd4&sig=W1kcjkWue-ttqCJHQLIK60AMSpo&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwidxsas-ITMAhUFJKYKHciPCNIQ6AEIRjAF#v=onepage&q=social%20mobility%20since%20the%2019th%20century&f=false), [here](http://www.bl.uk/romantics-and-victorians/articles/the-middle-classes-etiquette-and-upward-mobility) and [here](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=NFvGpa0CDp0C&pg=PA120&lpg=PA120&dq=%22post-industrial+society%22+social+mobility&source=bl&ots=uv8tOE7O_U&sig=gCgwJBXXwaFguaruleQK5kXlBrc&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjUlouM-4TMAhULpJQKHSLWDAkQ6AEISTAG#v=onepage&q=%22post-industrial%20society%22%20social%20mobility&f=false)\).
1.5.1. Pro: Industrial and post-industrial societies value educational attainment and become thereby more meritocratic \(see [here](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=q6_56x5tB7gC&pg=PA314&lpg=PA314&dq=%22post-industrial+society%22+social+mobility&source=bl&ots=2VRBnvMCCJ&sig=A4sa2_BU1Ufz6RyDK_lKrOwo9Ks&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwju7_Lzh4XMAhWMHpQKHbNrAJEQ6AEINjAD#v=onepage&q=%22post-industrial%20society%22%20social%20mobility&f=false), [here](http://soc.haifa.ac.il/~yaish/papers/SSR_Yaish&Andersen.pdf) and [here](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=u3rtCh-EUIIC&pg=PA198&lpg=PA198&dq=education+post-industrial+society+social+mobility&source=bl&ots=lRR_OhZaBt&sig=OEO1wphWBk2czxh00RI4MHX0lrs&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwiyz4v9iIXMAhUDJ5QKHd2-B0kQ6AEIYjAJ#v=onepage&q=education%20post-industrial%20society%20social%20mobility&f=false)\).
1.5.1.1. Con: Modern education systems [reproduce](https://www.um.edu.mt/__data/assets/pdf_file/0009/110232/van_Zanten-parents-inequality.pdf) [social inequalities](http://cdn.intechopen.com/pdfs-wm/34147.pdf), that is: educational attainment is largely determined by the socio-economic status and [especially](http://www.degruyter.com/dg/viewarticle.fullcontentlink:pdfeventlink/$002fj$002firsr.2015.5.issue-1$002firsr-2015-0004$002firsr-2015-0004.pdf/irsr-2015-0004.pdf?t:ac=j$002firsr.2015.5.issue-1$002firsr-2015-0004$002firsr-2015-0004.xml) education level of the parents.
1.5.1.2. Con: Education systems commonly reproduce elites with only selected institutions providing access, for example in [France](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=mcGgBgAAQBAJ&pg=PR2&dq=World+Yearbook+of+Education+2015&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwibpLPxjabMAhVIGpQKHXuLAugQ6AEIJzAA#v=onepage&q&f=false), [Britain](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=mcGgBgAAQBAJ&pg=PR2&dq=World+Yearbook+of+Education+2015&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwibpLPxjabMAhVIGpQKHXuLAugQ6AEIJzAA#v=onepage&q&f=false) and [Eastern Europe](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=aerFAAAAQBAJ&pg=PA12&dq=The+Open+World+and+Closed+Societies&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwiP6JWSjqbMAhUEkpQKHQ4vDEEQ6AEIHjAA#v=onepage&q&f=false).
1.5.2. Con: Upwards and downwards mobility are not exclusive; there have been marked periods of the latter, for example early in the 20th century [in Germany and Britain](https://books.google.co.kr/books?hl=de&lr=&id=RLBfzNkGfx8C&oi=fnd&pg=PR2&dq=A+Social+History+of+Twentieth-+Century+Europe&ots=zu62orIEOl&sig=qqKBxQB3PdcjV1RhMaBTNQx6TLg#v=onepage&q=A%20Social%20History%20of%20Twentieth-%20Century%20Europe&f=false), and since the end of the Cold War [in Eastern Europe](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=ifk5g0raMysC&pg=PR12&lpg=PR12&dq=Global+Trends+in+Eastern+Europe&source=bl&ots=Wf7GeDKTa1&sig=4qYJxl-hW5X5sCI5-5G-beswp7s&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjBv5Cyr5_MAhUlg4MKHTjGCEYQ6AEIKTAB#v=onepage&q=Global%20Trends%20in%20Eastern%20Europe&f=false).
1.5.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.2.1.1.
1.6. Con: Air, grounds and water were less clean in the 1990s as a result of increased pollution of the environment. Pollution caused many negative effects for society.
1.6.1. Con: Cities became cleaner by the 1990s. For a significant part of society this improved the environmental quality.
1.6.1.1. Pro: There were large [slums](http://www.sewerhistory.org/articles/whregion/finland/european_cities.pdf) in European cities in the 1890s.
1.6.1.2. Pro: In the 19th century there were repeated cholera outbreaks originating from [bad waste management](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_waste_management) in cities.
1.6.1.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.1.10.3.1.
1.6.1.3. Pro: [Incineration plants](https://books.google.co.uk/books?id=wUe4AwAAQBAJ&printsec=frontcover&hl=de&source=gbs_ge_summary_r&cad=0#v=onepage&q&f=false) with their damaging emissions were widespread in waste disposal management in major European cities.
1.6.1.4. Pro: [Toilet facilities](https://www.apstudynotes.org/european-history/outlines/chapter-24-life-in-the-changing-urban/) were close to non-existent in European cities in the 1890s.
1.6.1.5. Pro: [Water treatment improved](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_water_supply_and_sanitation#Modern_age) after the widespread use of water chlorination in the 20th century.
1.6.1.5.1. Pro: In [London](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_health#Epidemiology) water from sewage-polluted sections of the Thames was delivered to homes in the 19th century.
1.6.1.5.2. Pro: Diarrhea [declined](https://www.mtholyoke.edu/courses/rschwart/PDF/Industry,%20environment%20and%20health%20through%20200%20years%20in.pdf) significantly in Manchester in the 20th century. This indicates better water treatment.
1.6.1.6. Pro: In the 19th century people burned [coal](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=Pxg6Wg-12oYC&pg=PA292&lpg=PA292&dq=factories+1890+emissions&source=bl&ots=dKhaVslf38&sig=nOZwNRNkRVuJTeZ_eBU66zE1xrk&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwj8ytr2vofMAhUKppQKHXWcBhsQ6AEIPTAG#v=onepage&q&f=false) as a source of energy in the city. With the advent of alternatives the cities became cleaner in terms of air pollution.
1.6.1.7. Pro: In [London](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=Pxg6Wg-12oYC&pg=PA292&lpg=PA292&dq=factories+1890+emissions&source=bl&ots=dKhaVslf38&sig=nOZwNRNkRVuJTeZ_eBU66zE1xrk&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwj8ytr2vofMAhUKppQKHXWcBhsQ6AEIPTAG#v=onepage&q&f=false) in the late 19th century torches were required to walk on the streets because smoke was covering the sun.
1.6.2. Con: The water quality was much lower in the 1890s.
1.6.2.1. Pro: In industrialized societies of the 19th century, rivers were convenient disposal places without regard for the environment. This led to very dirty rivers.
1.6.3. Con: In the 1990s, most of the environmental polluting industries had been outsourced to developing countries.
1.6.4. Con: Individual factories were emitting more in the 1890s. This affected the immediate surroundings.
1.6.4.1. Pro: [Smog and soot](http://www.history.com/topics/water-and-air-pollution) had serious health impacts on nearby residents.
1.6.4.2. Pro: Absence of filter installations made emitted particles heavier and allows them to come down in closer distance to the factory.
1.6.4.3. Pro: Chimneys were lower in the 1890s. Thus the dirty exhaust could not be carried away far.
1.6.4.4. Pro: Because during the 1890s [coal](http://www.enviropedia.org.uk/Air_Quality/History.php) was used in factories, the emissions, such as [particulates](http://www.sourcewatch.org/index.php/Particulates_and_coal), were very decentralized. The change from coal to electricity in factories ended the unregulated decentralized coal combustion.
1.6.4.4.1. Pro: Coal consumption and [smog](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=Pxg6Wg-12oYC&pg=PA292&lpg=PA292&dq=factories+1890+emissions&source=bl&ots=dKhaVslf38&sig=nOZwNRNkRVuJTeZ_eBU66zE1xrk&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwj8ytr2vofMAhUKppQKHXWcBhsQ6AEIPTAG#v=onepage&q&f=false) is closely related in late 19th century London.
1.6.4.4.2. Pro: In the UK, the [National Smoke Abatement Institute](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=Pxg6Wg-12oYC&pg=PA292&lpg=PA292&dq=factories+1890+emissions&source=bl&ots=dKhaVslf38&sig=nOZwNRNkRVuJTeZ_eBU66zE1xrk&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwj8ytr2vofMAhUKppQKHXWcBhsQ6AEIPTAG#v=onepage&q&f=false) targeted the consumption of coal in factories as primary source of bad air quality in the city in the 1890s.
1.6.4.5. Pro: Factories were located mostly in the city which makes more people affected than if it would be on the countryside.
1.6.5. Pro: In 1890s people had not to worry about climate change with all its consequences.
1.6.5.1. Con: Worries of the people in the 1890s were of the same gravity or worse as in the 1990s.
1.6.5.1.1. Pro: Family, money and health dominate the agenda of every human in history. Thus, the worries of the 1890s were of the same gravity than those of 1990s.
1.6.5.2. Con: Not many people cared about climate change in the 1990s.
1.6.5.2.1. Con: The [Earth Summit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth_Summit) was held in 1992 and garnered global attention.
1.6.5.2.2. Con: The [IPCC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change) was formed in 1988 indicating global research about climate change resulting from worries about its effects.
1.6.5.2.3. Pro: [Skepticism](http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1002/wcc.321/pdf) about climate change became strong only in the late 2000s.
1.6.5.2.4. Con: Already in the 1990s climate change was a topic for which most of the population was either somewhat or very [concerned](http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1002/wcc.321/pdf).
1.6.5.3. Pro: Those living in the 1890s did not have to experience the consequences and thus did not have to worry about it.
1.6.5.4. Con: By the turn of the century the [garbage problem](http://www.ewp.rpi.edu/hartford/~ernesto/S2014/SHWPCE/Papers/SHW-Introduction/Crowell-HistoryofWaste.pdf) was seen as one of the greatest problems.
1.6.5.5. Pro: They did not have to worry, because they did not know about climate change back then.
1.6.5.6. Con: Instead of climate change the people were worrying about the environmental conditions in their immediate surroundings.
1.6.5.6.1. Pro: -> See 1.6.4.
1.6.5.7. Pro: In the 1890s there were no such things as carbon dioxide emissions lists / limit values.
1.6.5.7.1. Pro: The modern car was invented by [Benz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Car#Environmental_impact) in 1879. Only about 25 Benz vehicles were sold between 1888 and 1893, when his first four-wheeler was introduced. Thus there could not be much carbon dioxide emission back then.
1.6.5.8. Pro: In 1890s there were no such things as fracking or big oil platforms in the ocean.
1.6.5.9. Pro: In 1890s there were no such thing as refrigerators or hairsprays with CFC.
1.6.5.9.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.4.1.2.1.1.
1.6.6. Pro: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.1.3.4.1.8.3.1.
1.6.7. Pro: The use of [plastic / synthetic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plastic#Environmental_effects) materials \(highly resistant to most natural processes of degradation\) emerged in the 20th century, leading to an immense increase in energy requirement, carbon emissions and plastic waste.
1.6.8. Pro: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.4.1.2.1.1.
1.7. Con: Quality of life had decreased by the 1990s as intellectual cultural stimulation became shallower, due to \(serious\) arts and culture making way for \(simple\) entertainment.
1.7.1. Con: The rise of pop culture brought art and culture to new fields and contexts and made art and culture much more affordable, accessible and possible to participate in for everyone.
1.7.1.1. Pro: The gap between producer and consumer has been constantly narrowed by technological advancements.
1.7.1.1.1. Pro: The use of turntables has changed with Grandmaster Flash, who changed some cables within the turntables and the mixer to have possibilities to cue the other deck \(prelisten the song on the other turntable and therefore have advancement while mixing\).
1.7.1.1.2. Pro: Mass production of music instruments opened up the possibilities for musical education.
1.7.1.1.2.1. Con: Singing was possible without music instruments and was widespread before the mass production of music instruments.
1.7.1.1.3. Con: Because producers were more local in the 1890s and on a smaller base the gap between producers and consumers was smaller back then.
1.7.1.1.4. Pro: The rise of the [global internet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Internet#Rise_of_the_global_Internet_.28Late_1980s.2Fearly_1990s_onward.29) in the 1990s quickened this development significantly.
1.7.1.2. Pro: Programming became not only a hobby of nerds and known for boring business and administration applications, but showed it is possible to create games for a very broad audience.
1.7.1.2.1. Pro: Many popular games and characters, today considered an established part of pop culture, were developed in the 1990s.
1.7.1.2.1.1. Pro: [Yoshi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoshi) made its \(his?\) first appearance in the 1990s.
1.7.1.2.1.2. Pro: [Doom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doom_\(series\)) redefined the Ego-Shooter Genre in the 1990s.
1.7.1.2.1.3. Pro: The first GTA was developed in the 1990s.
1.7.1.2.1.4. Pro: [Guybrush Threepwood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guybrush_Threepwood) made his first appearance in the 1990s.
1.7.1.2.2. Con: Entertainment media merely replaced 1890's forms of entertainment and did not improve it.
1.7.1.2.2.1. Pro: Entertainment producing companies often stayed the same and only adapted to new technology.
1.7.1.2.2.1.1. Pro: Nintendo switched from being a toy and trading card company to being an all out videogames developer and hardware producer by the 1990s.
1.7.1.2.2.2. Pro: Many forms of entertainment were already existing in 1890.
1.7.1.2.2.2.1. Pro: [Cinema](http://www.vintageadbrowser.com/entertainment-ads-1890s) was already present in 1890.
1.7.1.2.2.2.1.1. Pro: [Travelling cinemas](http://www.lse.ac.uk/economicHistory/pdf/wp102.pdf) brought movies to the countryside already in the 1900s.
1.7.1.2.2.2.1.2. Con: It was mainly in the years [1905/1906](http://www.lse.ac.uk/economicHistory/pdf/wp102.pdf) that it is possible to speak of a cinema take off.
1.7.1.2.2.2.1.3. Con: Since the 1950s bigger screens were installed in cinemas, widescreen processes, polarized 3D projection and stereophonic sound were introduced.
1.7.1.2.2.2.2. Pro: Board games were very popular in the 1890s. Many of them famous until the 1990s.
1.7.1.2.2.2.2.1. Pro: [Chinese checkers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_checkers) was invented in 1892 and could be found in every games collection in 1990.
1.7.1.2.2.3. Pro: Famous novels of the 1890s were reproduced in the 1990s and live on as forms of entertainment indicating their high level of entertainment.
1.7.1.2.2.3.1. Con: Many famous novels, such as [Haruki Murakami](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haruki_Murakami)'s works, were not there in the 1890s.
1.7.1.2.2.3.2. Pro: The novel [Around the World in 80 Days](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Around_the_World_in_Eighty_Days#Film) was first published in 1873 but reproduced in the 1990s.
1.7.1.2.2.4. Con: In the 1890s consumer [expenditure](http://www.lse.ac.uk/economicHistory/pdf/wp102.pdf) for entertainment was relatively small.
1.7.1.2.2.5. Con: -> See 1.7.1.2.2.2.1.3.
1.7.1.2.2.6. Con: The introduction of "natural color" was a great development, which meant color that was photographically recorded from nature rather than added to black-and-white prints by hand-coloring, stencil-coloring or other arbitrary procedures.
1.7.1.2.2.7. Con: In the 1920s, the development of electronic sound recording technologies made it practical to incorporate a soundtrack of speech, music and sound effects synchronized with the action on the screen.
1.7.1.2.3. Con: Through standardization differences in individuals' entertainment knowledge reduces and makes entertainment less diverse in 1990 than in 1890.
1.7.1.2.3.1. Pro: Regional story-telling and local card games, or the personal stories of grandparents disappeared increasingly by the 1990.
1.7.1.2.3.1.1. Pro: Regional languages die with media integration and so do local stories disappear.
1.7.1.2.3.1.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.1.4.1.1.5.1.
1.7.1.2.3.1.1.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.2.1.4.1.1.5.2.
1.7.1.2.3.1.2. Pro: Families are increasingly affected by political events in the same way while in the past every family was able to tell an own story.
1.7.1.2.3.2. Con: Diversification of knowledge about the entertainment was guaranteed during the 1990s by an oversupply of entertainment.
1.7.1.2.4. Pro: -> See 1.7.1.2.2.1.1.
1.7.1.3. Con: Artists have become global icons that make them more distant, expensive and exclusive.
1.7.1.4. Con: A special feature of art is its appreciation. With mass production this appreciation vanishes and art renders itself an object of quotidian life.
1.7.2. Con: Modern technology allows for profound art forms, as can be found in the projects of [Dan Flavin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dan_Flavin).
1.7.3. Pro: Modern art works are often not distinguishable from the real items and thus added nothing anymore to arts and culture of the 1890s.
1.7.3.1. Pro: Warhol's [Brillo Box](http://www.warhol.org/education/resourceslessons/Aesthetics--Arthur-Danto/) could not be distinguished from a real box if it would be next to it.
1.7.3.2. Pro: Dan Flavin's [neon lights](https://www.pinterest.com/pin/300263500129669377/) are indistinguishable from New York subway lights.
1.7.3.3. Pro: Marcel [Duchamp](http://www.tate.org.uk/art/artworks/duchamp-fountain-t07573) exhibited a urinal as an artwork.
1.7.3.4. Con: Modern art forms, such as [Dada](http://www.theartstory.org/movement-dada.htm), make a point out of stretching the boundaries of what we consider art and producing "anti-art", for example by utilizing mundane objects. They intent to call into question what art is, and what purpose it serves for society. It intends to provoke [critical engagement with art](http://ir.uiowa.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?article=1262&context=dadasur); its achievement is visible in the very discussion we are having here.
1.7.3.4.1. Con: The Dada movement had ended by the 1990s.
1.7.3.4.1.1. Con: Dadaism is still highly influential in exhibitions and art sales, as [the prices of works](https://news.artnet.com/market/artnet-newss-top-10-expensive-living-american-artists-2015-323871) by Dada-inspired artists like Warhol, Koons and Wool illustrate.
1.7.3.4.2. Con: Dada [artworks](http://www.theartstory.org/movement-dada-artworks.htm#pnt_2) were generally distinguishable from normal products.
1.7.4. Pro: Many modern pieces of art are not easy to see as art and therefore need some institutional [framework](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_art#Institutional) to be declared and recognized as such, e.g. in a museum. This means art in itself becomes irrelevant without a frame.
1.7.4.1. Con: Movements like [street art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Street_art) that took art out of that framework were established in the 1980s.
1.7.4.1.1. Con: Not every graffiti becomes street art. Only through the recognition of the art after artists like Banksy some paintings had the possibility to transform into art.
1.7.4.1.1.1. Pro: Graffiti can be considered [vandalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vandalism).
1.7.4.1.1.1.1. Pro: Banksy himself was hiding from the [police](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banksy#Early_career_.281992.E2.80.932001.29).
1.7.4.1.1.2. Con: Graffiti was considered a form of art long before Banksy.
1.7.4.1.1.3. Con: Graffiti becomes street art through its existence. The recognition as art does not depend on per- or reception by other artists but, as with every art, by the individual himself.
1.7.4.1.1.3.1. Con: Graffiti is not street art. Graffiti is an unique sub-cultural movement, that can at best seen as a kind of prototype of street art, but it has way more rules and internal rule sets than street art in particular or art in general has.
1.7.4.1.1.3.1.1. Con: One of the people changing those rulesets of graffiti culture was Shepard Fairey, better known as Obey, who started the transformation with his [Andre the Giant has a posse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andre_the_Giant_Has_a_Posse) campaign.
1.7.4.1.1.3.1.2. Con: Graffiti and Street Art are very close and belong together, together they can be subsumed as Urban Art, which shows in the emergence of Art fairs such as the [Urban Art Fair](http://urbanartfair.fr/en/) in Paris or the [Stroke Artfair](http://www.stroke-artfair.com/) in Munich/Berlin.
1.7.4.1.1.3.1.3. Con: Graffiti and Street Art are shown as at least complementary in [one](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marc_Eck%C5%8D%27s_Getting_Up:_Contents_Under_Pressure) of the two video games on the topic which have to be taken serious.
1.7.4.1.1.4. Con: -> See 1.7.4.1.1.3.1.
1.7.4.1.2. Con: Most graffitis are not standing alone but their ensemble is considered as art work, such as the East Side Gallery. Thus, the individual piece is no art.
1.7.4.1.2.1. Con: Artists like [Banksy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banksy) create pieces that do not need an ensemble.
1.7.4.1.2.2. Con: Due to the lack of allowed spaces and the history of Graffiti \(which is embraced by those who just keep it in illegal spaces\) what we see as "ensembles" with greater context in reality is just called a "Hall of Fame" where local graffiti artists have legal spaces to write on walls. But there is no overarching theme or concept in general, just the assembly of individual pieces.
1.7.4.1.2.2.1. Con: This does not apply to the example of the East Side Gallery in Berlin, which is an ensemble and was designed as such.
1.7.4.1.2.2.1.1. Pro: The East Side Gallery is one of the most influential graffiti art exhibitions in the world.
1.7.4.2. Pro: The success of art does not rely on its aesthetic qualities anymore, but first and foremost on endorsement by the art world: ["Without institutional support the artist is doomed and art becomes non sequitur](https://books.google.co.kr/books/about/The_Key_Issues_Concerning_Contemporary_A.html?id=68Ia-Al0RRIC&redir_esc=y)".
1.7.4.3. Con: The vast majority of art consumed in 1990 was consumer art - movies, comics, video games - that is accessible via the open market and not in need of any institutional framework.
1.7.4.3.1. Pro: "Art itself" adopts very fast to new technologies and finds its way to the audience.
1.7.5. Pro: There is no more [progress](http://hyperallergic.com/191329/an-illustrated-guide-to-arthur-dantos-the-end-of-art/) in art as it has disintegrated into a cluster of competing approaches and understandings of what 'art' means.
1.7.5.1. Con: -> See 1.7.3.4.
1.7.6. Pro: TV was an major cultural asset, entertaining people on a broad but rather shallow level.
1.7.6.1. Pro: Watching TV reduces the time to read [books](https://www.dcmp.org/caai/nadh175.pdf).
1.7.6.1.1. Pro: The brain could be said to be in an hypnotical situation when watching tv, causing it more relaxing to do as an activity in comparison with the activity of reading, which requires an higher level of concentration
1.7.6.2. Pro: The spread of TV [accelerated](http://www.barb.co.uk/resources/tv-facts/tv-ownership) between 1950s and 1990s. This added TV as a qualitative asset for entertainment.
1.7.6.2.1. Con: TV [addiction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Television_addiction) prevents individuals from partaking in social life and makes them feel less happy.
1.7.6.2.1.1. Con: Individuals that feel socially isolated can make use of TV to stay connected with society by creating [imaginary friends](http://www.scientificamerican.com/article/imaginary-friends/).
1.7.6.2.1.1.1. Con: Imaginary friends do not help to stay connected with society but rather deepen social exclusion as they reduce the pressure to connect with others in real life.
1.7.6.2.1.2. Pro: TV consumption is comparable to [hypnosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_aspects_of_television#Psychological_effects) because it only encourages activity on the right side of the brain.
1.7.6.2.1.3. Con: TV programmes can be beneficial to social life, e.g. in times of huge sports events like the upcoming UEFA European Championship.
1.7.6.2.2. Con: Watching TV makes people more [aggressive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_aspects_of_television#Alleged_dangers).
1.7.6.2.3. Pro: -> See 1.7.6.2.1.3.
1.7.6.2.4. Pro: People who are watching TV do not need to leave their house to be entertained if they do not want to.
1.7.6.2.5. Con: TV consumption makes dull because the brain creates [dopamine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_aspects_of_television#Psychological_effects).
1.7.6.2.6. Con: TV creates blurred imaginations about reality.
1.7.6.2.6.1. Pro: TV consumption is influencing [work](http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/j.1559-1816.2008.00436.x/full) behavior and expectations.
1.7.6.2.6.2. Pro: [Casting](http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/DawsonCasting) of young adults in their mid-20s for teenage roles creates unrealistic imaginations about the appearance of teenagers.
1.7.6.2.6.3. Pro: TV created [images](http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/RealityIsUnrealistic) of items, landscapes, skills and behaviors that do not resemble reality, e.g. White Christmas or that the heart is so far on the left.
1.7.6.2.6.4. Pro: [Reality TV](http://www.parents-choice.org/article.cfm?art_id=313&the_page=editorials) creates an image of 'reality' that is unrealistic and emphasizes competitiveness, immature behavior and distorted reward systems.
1.7.6.2.6.5. Pro: [Dating](http://www.bustle.com/articles/119286-90s-sitcom-dating-vs-real-life-will-make-that-decades-tv-seem-so-unrealistic) expectations of the 1990s were shaped by sitcoms.
1.7.6.2.7. Pro: TV is helping [education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Educational_television) of citizens and therewith increase their life quality.
1.7.6.2.7.1. Pro: Because TV is a very [accessible](https://www.dcmp.org/caai/nadh175.pdf) medium, it reaches learners that have not been able to participate in traditional adult literacy programs.
1.7.6.2.7.2. Pro: Even though it might not increase mental well-being, education does prevent mental [illness](http://www2.warwick.ac.uk/newsandevents/pressreleases/education_may_not/).
1.7.6.2.7.3. Con: -> See 1.7.6.1.
1.7.6.2.7.4. Pro: Educational TV [programs](https://www.dcmp.org/caai/nadh175.pdf) help adults and children to develop their skills in a convenient way.
1.7.6.2.8. Pro: Of the top 20 TV programmes screened in the UK in 1990, there were [19](http://www.bfi.org.uk/sites/bfi.org.uk/files/downloads/bfi-the-stats-an-overview-of-the-film-television-video-and-dvd-industries-in-the-uk-1990-2003.pdf) entertainment programs.
1.7.6.3. Con: -> See 1.7.6.2.7.
1.7.6.4. Pro: -> See 1.7.6.2.5.
1.7.7. Con: There was still more than enough "serious" arts and culture in Europe in the 1990s. Just because there is simple entertainment now, does not mean that art and culture is gone.
1.7.7.1. Pro: Modern art forms emerged in the 20th century.
1.7.7.1.1. Pro: [Minimalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minimalism) is a distinct form of art and made contribution to the city spaces and [living environment](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/lifestyle/interiors/11539508/A-Parisian-architect-does-liveable-minimalism.html) of the people of Europe.
1.7.7.2. Con: The art forms that sprung in the early 20th century, like surrealism or dadaism, emerged out of the proto-avantgarde movement at the turn of the century. There is no comparable thing for the late 20th century.
1.7.7.2.1. Pro: [Marinetti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filippo_Tommaso_Marinetti) is one of the founding fathers of modern European art forms and was most active in the early 1900s.
1.7.7.3. Pro: The richness of city architecture is bigger today than it was in the 19th century given the different styles that integrate with each other.
1.7.7.4. Pro: European cities spend billions every year on museums, theatres and philharmonic orchestras, many of them easily among the best in the world in their department.
1.7.8. Con: New forms of arts and culture were, in the beginning, very often seen as profane and simple entertainment regardless of their qualities. This was the case with Jazz, Rock and Roll, or Pop. Thus, it seems to be a defensive stance rather than a qualitative measure.
1.7.8.1. Pro: "Seriousness" lies in the eye of the beholder. Songs by musicians like David Bowie or Bob Dylan were seen as total scrap by fans of classical music.
1.7.8.2. Pro: Art forms expand building upon each other, making new developments appear to be of low quality. From hindsight, however, we can see that they were crucial building blocks in the [formation of modern art](http://makezine.com/2013/11/15/art-technology-new-art-forms-not-just-new-art/).
1.8. Con: Europe was at the climax of its power with its colonial empire at the end of the 19th century. Spillover effects from this position of power benefited citizens in their daily lives and decreased since then.
1.8.1. Con: By 1890 the United States had [overtaken all European powers](https://books.google.co.kr/books/about/Power_Transitions_Strategies_For_the_21s.html?id=xEF3AAAAMAAJ&redir_esc=y), Russia as well as China in terms of economic output and international power.
1.8.1.1. Con: The capabilities of the US did not transform into power because the [institutional](http://press.princeton.edu/titles/6306.html) set-up prevented an extraction of resources for foreign policy conduct.
1.8.1.2. Con: In the 1890s the US themselves thought to lack behind the race for imperialism and battleships.
1.8.2. Pro: In the 1890s it was a time of great technological advancement that changed the life of people. The technology of the 1990s is nothing in comparison.
1.8.2.1. Con: The so called third great wave of inventions, [the digital revolution](http://www.economist.com/news/special-report/21621156-first-two-industrial-revolutions-inflicted-plenty-pain-ultimately-benefited), took place in late 20th century and changed people's life strongly and significantly.
1.8.2.1.1. Pro: [New technologies](http://www.economist.com/news/special-report/21621156-first-two-industrial-revolutions-inflicted-plenty-pain-ultimately-benefited), like the omnipresent internet, advanced robotics and machine intelligence were developed.
1.8.2.1.1.1. Con: Many new technologies could not show their full potential during the 1990s and would need more time to develop.
1.8.2.1.1.1.1. Pro: Until the year 2000 only about [4%](http://www.internetworldstats.com/emarketing.htm) of the world population used the internet.
1.8.2.1.1.1.1.1. Con: If these 4% are concentrated in Europe and the US then this is sufficient to have a thriving internet industry.
1.8.2.2. Pro: There is [no comparable innovation](https://www.foreignaffairs.com/reviews/review-essay/2016-02-15/innovation-over) that revolutionized individual life's as did the inventions at the end of the 19th century.
1.8.2.2.1. Pro: The steam engine, the locomotive, the telephone, the telegraph, the internal combustion engine, electrical light - all these inventions came out of the 19th century and laid the foundation for the unprecedented growth of the 20th century.
1.8.2.2.2. Con: [Productivity](http://piketty.pse.ens.fr/files/CetteEtal09.pdf) grew at a faster pace between 1950 and 1980 than it did between 1890 and 1950. This indicates that the major contributions and innovations took place in the second half of the 20th century.
1.8.3. Pro: Colonies have provided material benefits to the citizens of Europe.
1.8.3.1. Pro: For the UK the opium trade between its colony India and China was of major importance and channeled much silver to Westminster.
1.8.3.1.1. Con: During the period of New Imperialism - which the 1890s are part of - colonies had generally become unprofitable for colonial powers and a burden on their tax payers \(see [here](http://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1111/1468-0335.00092/abstract) and [here](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=94e1PxsJrOoC&printsec=frontcover&dq=Mammon+and+the+Pursuit+of+Empire&hl=en&sa=X&redir_esc=y#v=onepage&q=unprofitable&f=false)\).
1.8.3.2. Pro: Between 1830 and 1870, 1 billion guilders were taken from [Indonesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies#Economic_history), on average making 25 per cent of the annual Dutch Government budget.
1.8.3.3. Con: Products produced in former colonies are still available.
1.8.3.4. Con: Cheap labor from migrant workers is still available.
1.8.4. Pro: Europeans enjoyed a feeling of superiority towards the rest of the world.
1.8.4.1. Pro: White men were treated like masters in the colonies.
1.8.4.2. Pro: Europeans saw themselves at the top of the hierarchy of civilizations, lived with a notion "[racial, cultural, scientific and technological superiority](http://ieg-ego.eu/en/threads/backgrounds/european-encounters/guido-abbattista-european-encounters-in-the-age-of-expansion)", and saw it as their mission to civilize other peoples.
1.8.4.3. Con: For European women this reduced feeling of cultural supremacy has created benefits because their role model changed.
1.8.4.3.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.2.1.
1.8.4.3.2. Pro: Women do less [housework](http://www.soc.umn.edu/~elkelly/Bianchietal2000HouseworkTrends.pdf) while men do more.
1.8.4.3.3. Con: Women have lost equally a status they once enjoyed as [role models](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=JgZ2_QFbEmMC&printsec=frontcover&source=gbs_ge_summary_r&cad=0#v=onepage&q&f=false) for women in colonized societies.
1.8.5. Con: It was in the Spanish-American war in 1898 that a European power was the first time defeated by a non-European power since industrial modernization.
1.8.5.1. Con: The US was seen as kind of European power. The first shock for Europeans was the defeat of Russia against Japan in 1905.
1.8.5.2. Pro: The [decline of the Spanish Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War) was a shock to the Spaniards and their understanding of superiority.
1.9. Con: The world for Europeans was safer in the 1890s than it was in the 1990s.
1.9.1. Pro: In the 1890s, Europeans were able to enjoy considerable [extraterritoriality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extraterritoriality#East_Asia) rights which made it safer for them if they committed a crime in another country outside Europe.
1.9.1.1. Con: Extraterritoriality was enjoyed by a small fraction of Europeans only.
1.9.2. Con: Improved communication and transportation systems made life safer as rescue teams and police are easier to contact and can better coordinate among themselves. This eventually saves lives.
1.9.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.1.10.
1.9.4. Pro: Terrorism had emerged by 1990s, spreading a feeling of insecurity that did not exist in 1890.
1.9.4.1. Pro: Technological developments made terrorism more threatening.
1.9.4.1.1. Pro: With technological developments in explosives it became easier to inflict mass casualties.
1.9.4.1.1.1. Pro: The increased availability of chemicals has allowed the construction of [improvised explosive devices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Improvised_explosive_device).
1.9.4.1.1.2. Pro: [Dynamite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamite) was only invented in the second half of the 19th century and spread afterwards.
1.9.4.1.1.3. Pro: [C-4 explosive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C-4_%28explosive%29) was just invented in 1956.
1.9.4.1.1.4. Pro: [PENT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pentaerythritol_tetranitrate#Terrorist_use) was used in terrorist attacks since 1983.
1.9.4.1.2. Pro: More effective firearms made terrorism quicker, less detectable, and more devastating.
1.9.4.1.2.1. Pro: Early [gatling guns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_gun#Early_rapid-firing_weapons) had the size of contemporary artillery but developed into portable machine guns in the 20th century.
1.9.4.1.2.2. Pro: The first [semi-automatic firearms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-automatic_firearm) were developed in the early 20th century giving terrorist easier access to cheap and effective firearms.
1.9.4.1.2.3. Con: The [revolver](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolver) was already widespread in the 19th century.
1.9.4.1.2.4. Pro: In the 19th century [single-shot firearms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single-shot#History) were mostly used only. This makes terrorist attacks back then slower and less devastating.
1.9.4.1.3. Pro: With better media coverage terrorist attacks became threatening to Europeans even if they are not committed on European soil.
1.9.4.1.3.1. Con: Attacks on Europeans in colonies were seen as threatening by 19th century Europeans.
1.9.4.1.3.1.1. Pro: When Opium traders in early 19th century China were attacked by anti-foreign mobs, businesses in the [UK](http://books.wwnorton.com/books/Commissioner-Lin-and-the-Opium-War/) felt threatened and pressured for military intervention.
1.9.4.1.3.2. Pro: After the [Oklahoma City bombing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oklahoma_City_bombing#International_reaction) in 1995 Europeans were shocked and indicated sympathy with the victims.
1.9.4.1.3.3. Pro: The 1993 [World Trade Centre Bombing](https://www.stratfor.com/weekly/look-back-1993-world-trade-center-bombing) was broadcasted in Europe spreading a sense of insecurity.
1.9.4.1.3.4. Pro: [Fictional popular culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gelignite#Use_in_popular_culture) of terrorist attacks spread a feeling of insecurity regardless of whether these were commited in reality.
1.9.4.2. Pro: The intensity of terrorism increased and made it more threatening.
1.9.4.2.1. Pro: In the 1990s the first signs of  [Islamic terrorism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_terrorism#Late_20th_century) started to threaten the population.
1.9.4.2.2. Pro: The emergence of widespread indiscriminate [terrorism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_terrorism#Early_20th_century) is bound to the emergence of revolutionary nationalism in the 20th century.
1.9.4.3. Pro: By the 1990s there had already emerged a new form of terrorism \(mostly due to globalization\): international terrorism.
1.9.4.3.1. Pro: "New" forms of terrorism are very often driven by religion, thus nationality by logic has to play a smaller role.
1.9.4.3.1.1. Pro: In contrast, terrorism in the 19th century was often motivated by [nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalist_terrorism), such as [Narodnaya Volya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narodnaya_Volya) or the [Black Hand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Hand_\(Serbia\)). Thus the motivation changed.
1.9.4.3.1.2. Pro: -> See 1.9.4.2.1.
1.9.4.3.2. Con: Europe did not experience many terror attacks in the 1990s.
1.9.4.3.2.1. Pro: There were only two attacks that targeted citizens in a nondiscriminatory way.
1.9.4.3.2.1.1. Con: -> See 1.9.4.2.1.
1.9.4.3.2.1.2. Pro: The [1995 Paris Metro bombings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1995_Paris_M%C3%A9tro_and_RER_bombings) were targeting civilians.
1.9.4.3.2.1.3. Pro: The [1998 Omagh Bombing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omagh_bombing) killed 39 random citizens.
1.9.4.4. Con: Terror was already widespread in Europe in 1890.
1.9.4.4.1. Pro: The first recorded act of terrorism in the civil society was the assassination of Jean Paul Marat by Charlotte Corday. The risk of terrorism therefore was already present almost 100 years in Europe before the 1890s.
1.9.4.4.1.1. Con: Jean Paul Marat's [assassination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlotte_Corday#Marat.27s_assassination) was done with a hidden blade which is a fundamental different method than bombing innocent people.
1.9.4.4.1.2. Pro: Assassinations of political opponents were quite normal in all of humanity's history.
1.9.4.4.2. Pro: In Germany, as a reaction to the terrorist murder of August von Kotzebue, the [Carlsbad Decrees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carlsbad_Decrees#Investigating_Committee) were introduced in 1819. They resembled anti-terror laws of today. Thus, terror did not seem to be a French phenomenon, even more that Germany by the time they were introduced had not experienced a revolution like France.
1.9.4.4.3. Con: Terror was targeted on politically agitating individuals in 1890 while it became nondiscriminatory in the 1990s.
1.9.4.4.3.1. Pro: -> See 1.9.4.3.2.1.2.
1.9.4.4.3.2. Pro: -> See 1.9.4.3.2.1.3.
1.9.4.4.3.3. Con: Terrorism got a new meaning in the times of civil society, having the focus not only on specific targets, but the aftermath on chosen societal spheres. Thus the nondiscriminatory factor does not matter, because for the targeted spheres, who are intended to be brought into upheaval, are still the same, regardless of who specifically got killed.
1.9.4.4.3.3.1. Con: When terrorists only kill political targets all non-political persons can feel safe. This is different if terrorists kill nondiscriminatory.
1.9.4.5. Con: -> See 1.9.4.3.2.
1.9.5. Pro: By 1990, the threat of nuclear annihilation had developed.
1.9.5.1. Con: Nuclear annihilation was [not a practical possibility or actual threat](https://www.mtholyoke.edu/acad/intrel/waltz1.htm) due to the certainty of mutually assured destruction.
1.9.5.1.1. Con: Many people [feared](http://blogs.scientificamerican.com/guest-blog/the-rise-of-nuclear-fear-how-we-learned-to-fear-the-bomb/) nuclear annihilation regardless of whether it was imagined or real.
1.9.5.1.2. Con: Nuclear wars can start by accident.
1.9.5.1.2.1. Pro: An accidentally nuclear detonation in a highly tensed situation can be misinterpreted and lead to war.
1.9.5.1.2.2. Pro: Nuclear equipped powers can be dragged into an initially smaller war and feel compelled to make use of nuclear weapons there.
1.9.5.1.3. Con: Mutually assured destruction is of no help to most Europeans who live in countries that do not have nuclear weapons.
1.9.5.1.3.1. Con: All Europeans live under the nuclear umbrella of NATO and the EU. Several large European countries - such as Germany and Italy - without their own nuclear weapons even have American nuclear weapons stationed on their territory.
1.9.5.1.3.1.1. Con: The EU does not provide security guarantees.
1.9.5.1.3.1.1.1. Con: In case of doubt there will be strong normative pressure to assist an attacked member state.
1.9.5.1.3.1.1.1.1. Pro: When [France](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/paris-terror-eu-countries-pledge-military-support-as-france-and-russia-launch-new-air-strikes-on-a6738511.html) perceived to be under attack by ISIS terrorism EU states rushed to support it.
1.9.5.1.3.1.2. Con: Eastern European countries experience a fear of abandonment.
1.9.5.1.3.1.3. Con: Not all EU members are members of NATO.
1.9.5.1.3.1.4. Pro: The states of Western Europe  - among them two nuclear powers - were [part of the Western European Union](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=GsyhCgAAQBAJ&pg=PA305&dq=Historical+Dictionary+of+the+European+Union&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjR4MfhgZ_MAhWmnqYKHWR8AMkQ6AEIJDAB#v=onepage&q=%22Western%20European%20Union%22&f=false) from 1954 to 2010 which included a mutual defense clause.
1.9.5.1.4. Pro: Not a single nuclear weapon was deployed with aggressive intent since 1945. Even confrontations of great powers - such as the Cuban Missile Crisis and the Korean War - did not feature their use.
1.9.5.1.4.1. Con: The world came to nuclear annihilation several times.
1.9.5.1.4.1.1. Pro: Strategic [bombers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strategic_bomber#The_Cold_War_and_its_aftermath) were constantly in the air to retaliate.
1.9.5.1.4.1.2. Pro: Nuclear weapons played a strategic role during the Korean War when it was transferred to [Guam](http://www.pbs.org/wgbh/amex/bomb/peopleevents/pandeAMEX58.html) to be deployed quickly.
1.9.5.2. Con: By the 1990s the Cold War was over and therefore the main source of nuclear annihilation, the UdSSR, had been defeated.
1.9.5.2.1. Con: While the Soviet Union had a tight grip on its nuclear materials, [a lack of security surrounding them](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=kcuJvl8FcBIC&printsec=frontcover&dq=Transnational+Threats:+Smuggling+and+Trafficking+in+Arms,+Drugs,+and+Human+Life&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwiL_r_455bMAhUlxqYKHVqvDAUQ6AEIGzAA#v=onepage&q&f=false) became a new, possibly even greater danger after the Soviet Union's demise.
1.9.5.2.1.1. Con: Loose nukes pose less a threat of nuclear annihilation for humankind than the Cold War stand-off.
1.9.5.3. Pro: By the 1990s there were several atomic powers existing: USA, Russia, France, Great Britain, China, India, Pakistan and Israel.
1.9.5.3.1. Pro: Nuclear weapons have spread to politically unstable states, for example Pakistan which experienced stagflation during the 1990s, a military coup in 1999 as well as an unsuccessful coup attempt in 1995.
1.9.5.4. Pro: During the 1890s people did not suffer from the fears and anxieties that nuclear technology [caused as part of the "risk society"](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=lqyBAgAAQBAJ&printsec=frontcover&dq=Anxiety+in+a+%27Risk%27+Society&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwiwl4bN15bMAhUCFqYKHS8hBDkQ6AEIHjAA#v=onepage&q=Anxiety%20in%20a%20'Risk'%20Society&f=false) of the 1990's.
1.9.6. Pro: -> See 1.1.3.4.
1.9.7. Con: Military technologies were better regulated by the 1990s.
1.9.7.1. Con: International law already prohibited the use of chemical weapons by 1899, under the [Hague Convention](https://www.opcw.org/chemical-weapons-convention/related-international-agreements/chemical-warfare-and-chemical-weapons/hague-convention-of-1899/).
1.9.7.1.1. Con: Chemical weapons were used despite the prohibition, for example in [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_weapons_in_World_War_I).
1.9.7.2. Pro: The [Chemical Weapons Convention \(CWC\)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_Weapons_Convention) has been signed and ratified by the vast majority of states and outlaws the production, stockpiling and use of chemical weapons.
1.9.7.2.1. Pro: Chemical Weapons have [not been used](https://www.opcw.org/about-chemical-weapons/history-of-cw-use/) in inter-state warfare since the 1980s \(by Iraq against Iran\).
1.9.7.3. Pro: The [Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty \(NPT\)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Non-Proliferation_of_Nuclear_Weapons) has been signed and ratified by most states, successfully limited the spread of nuclear weapons and established an international regime that monitors states' nuclear capacities.
1.9.7.3.1. Con: Nuclear weapons did not even exit back in the 1890s, thus a regulation of such technology was not necessary.
1.9.7.4. Pro: The [Biological Weapons Convention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_Weapons_Convention) \(BWC\) banning the production of biological weapons is one example where the spread of a technology was successfully stopped before it came to be used on a large scale.
1.9.7.5. Con: Conventions and treaties \(related immediately to such weapons or their aftermaths, like the [Budapest Memorandum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Budapest_Memorandum_on_Security_Assurances)\) are nice to have on paper, but in practice they do not prevent signatory states from breaking the rules.
1.9.7.5.1. Pro: -> See 1.9.7.1.1.
1.9.8. Con: -> See 1.1.7.3.1.5.
1.9.9. Con: Street lighting in 1890 was poor compared to 1990
1.9.10. Con: Industrial machines were rarely guarded, and behaved less reliably or predictably in 1890 and so claimed more lives
1.9.11. Con: More people per capita died doing work in 1890 than in 1990

1.13. Pro: Progress in the transportation sector made the quality of life better in the 1990s.
1.13.1. Pro: Transportation of overseas fruits was better in the 1990s than it was in the 1890s.
1.13.1.1. Pro: The impact of CO² and O² on [respiration](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=Q4C0Pxm3RvkC&pg=PA98&lpg=PA98&dq=Ethylene+production+19th+century&source=bl&ots=Ij3kCQfzI8&sig=KwgODOvzutPXq-mV1rMtpJC--q4&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjOwaDCl9XLAhXFIqYKHcf3Dx4Q6AEIKTAC#v=onepage&q=Ethylene%20production%2019th%20century&f=false) of plants was not yet fully understood by the end of the 19th century. This made it more difficult to transport fruits properly.
1.13.1.2. Pro: The effects of [ethylene](http://ucanr.edu/datastoreFiles/608-355.pdf) were not yet known. This made it difficult to harvest green bananas for shipping because ethylene is used to make them [yellow](http://cwh.ucsc.edu/bananas/Site/Modern%20History%20of%20the%20Banana.html) again.
1.13.1.3. Pro: The [supply chains](http://cwh.ucsc.edu/bananas/Site/Modern%20History%20of%20the%20Banana.html) between producers and consumers were not as effective and required more time. This made shipping more difficult because fruits ripened in between.
1.13.1.3.1. Pro: Farmers [harvested](http://cwh.ucsc.edu/bananas/Site/Modern%20History%20of%20the%20Banana.html) plantains ripe, thus making it susceptible to bruising and spoilage on journeys, especially those of long distance.
1.13.1.4. Pro: [Roads](http://cwh.ucsc.edu/bananas/Site/Modern%20History%20of%20the%20Banana.html) from plantations to harbors were of lower quality often leading to bruises of the produce.

1.16. Con: Between the 1890s and the 1990s, human life has become more distanced from the life humanity had before the advent of industrialization.
1.16.1. Con: Humans' understanding of sex and their body became less strained and more natural.

1.16.1.3.1. Pro: The protests of 1968 transformed social understanding of body and politics to be more enlightened.
1.16.1.3.1.1. Pro: In France the 1968 protests started with a demand by students to be allowed to [sleep together](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/egalit-libert-sexualit-paris-may-1968-784703.html).

1.16.1.3.1.3. Pro: In the early 1960s, the sexual liberation movement was aided by [feminist ideologues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_revolution#Feminism_and_sexual_liberation) in their mutual struggle to challenge traditional ideas regarding female sexuality.
1.16.1.3.1.3.1. Pro: The book '[The Sensuous Woman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Sensuous_Woman)' was the first detailed instruction manual concerning sexuality for women and published in 1969.
1.16.1.3.1.3.1.1. Con: [Fanny Hill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fanny_Hill) was already written in the 18th century and described sexual pleasures of women in detail.

1.16.1.3.1.4. Pro: The sexual liberation thrive was aided by the discovery of the pill as a tool for contraception. This allowed more people to sleep with each other than before.
1.16.1.3.1.4.1. Pro: In the UK [the pill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_revolution#United_Kingdom) became free of charge for any woman in 1968.

1.16.1.3.1.8. Con: The sexual revolution of the 1960s did not actually lead to sex being enjoyed freely, it is [just observed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_revolution#Criticism) in all the fields of culture.
1.16.1.4. Pro: Sexual [ignorance](http://www.independent.co.uk/life-style/love-sex/culture-of-love/a-brief-cultural-history-of-sex-938527.html) and misleading ideals turned the 19th century into the most rotten age there has ever been for sexuality.
1.16.2. Con: Infanticide was widespread across the continent in the 19th century. This shows that newborns were regarded with less value than in the 1990s.
1.16.2.1. Con: In the UK, between 1880 and 1900 the number of children born reduced significantly and so did the number of [infanticide](http://www.jstor.org/stable/2173842?seq=1#page_scan_tab_contents).

1.16.2.3. Con: In the 19th century, high child mortality was the result of [Sudden Infant Death Syndrome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudden_infant_death_syndrome) rather than [infanticide](http://www.jstor.org/stable/2173842?seq=1#page_scan_tab_contents).

1.16.3. Con: The idea "natural state" is an intellectual concept and not itself natural. Thus there cannot be a value hierarchy between a "natural" and an "unnatural" state.
1.16.3.1. Pro: To determine something as "natural" has the function of morally distinguishing between "good" and "bad". And  without this distinction human action could not be directed towards an end and would result in chaos \(cf. Hobbes' bellum omnies contra omnes, where this distinction has not yet been made, and everything counts as "natural".\)
1.16.3.1.1. Con: The attribute "natural" by no means always has a positive connotation. 1.16.7. Con: In 1890 the natural connection between nature and human was already ruptured by a century of industrial modernization.

1.16.8.1.2. Pro: It became increasingly frequent to call a medical doctor instead of a pastor for someone who attempted to commit [suicide](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=Zi-xoFAPnPMC&pg=PA128&lpg=PA128&dq=suicide+rate+1900&source=bl&ots=DDE5W4gbkv&sig=itYeiU1X6rT5asqKCZum4bbubwY&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjc4J2jmu7KAhWCEpQKHaG3CXkQ6AEIXTAH#v=onepage&q&f=false).
1.16.8.2. Pro: Death of the elderly has been taken out of the family context into the [health industry](https://exopermaculture.com/2016/01/19/how-we-used-to-die-how-we-die-now/).
1.16.8.3. Pro: The progress of the hospital system [separates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Birth_of_the_Clinic#The_medical_gaze) the patient's body from the patient's identity because physicians started to see the body as seperate field of research.
1.16.8.3.1. Pro: Because of numerous patients the individual is seen as part of a [wider group](http://static1.squarespace.com/static/51e3f4ede4b053e5f0062efd/t/51f7e4bae4b088f41b103013/1375200442047/dehumanization-in-medicine.pdf) and deindividualized.
1.16.8.3.2. Pro: In a hospital patients are not structuring their day themselves but the planners, patients experience a loss in agency that leads to [dehumanization](http://static1.squarespace.com/static/51e3f4ede4b053e5f0062efd/t/51f7e4bae4b088f41b103013/1375200442047/dehumanization-in-medicine.pdf).
1.16.8.3.3. Pro: Patients are not very similar to physicians because they are ill and have less power. This causes [dehumanization](http://static1.squarespace.com/static/51e3f4ede4b053e5f0062efd/t/51f7e4bae4b088f41b103013/1375200442047/dehumanization-in-medicine.pdf) of patients because the need to consult the patient diminished and the experience of power leads him to treat patients as a means to an end.
1.16.8.3.4. Pro: Increasing [mechanization](http://static1.squarespace.com/static/51e3f4ede4b053e5f0062efd/t/51f7e4bae4b088f41b103013/1375200442047/dehumanization-in-medicine.pdf) of processes necessary for medical treatment distances the patient from the physician and leads to dehumanization.
1.16.8.3.5. Pro: Because physicians who work in a hospital show [less empathy](http://static1.squarespace.com/static/51e3f4ede4b053e5f0062efd/t/51f7e4bae4b088f41b103013/1375200442047/dehumanization-in-medicine.pdf) for their patients there is a process of dehumanization.
1.16.8.3.6. Pro: Because physicians are likely to cause pain to the patient, dehumanization helps to create a [moral gap](http://static1.squarespace.com/static/51e3f4ede4b053e5f0062efd/t/51f7e4bae4b088f41b103013/1375200442047/dehumanization-in-medicine.pdf) necessary for the physician.
1.16.8.4. Pro: The need for the establishment of such institutions speaks a clear language for the negative impact humans have had on natural processes.
1.16.8.5. Con: In 1890, humans have been exhibited as [zoological objects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_zoo#1870s_to_World_War_II). This was not the case in 1990 anymore.
1.16.8.5.1. Con: In the 1990s Europeans stepped up their game, came up with a [TV show](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_Brother_\(franchise\)) and put humans under permanent surveillance, called out a price money for the last remaining inhabitant and let viewers decide who has to leave the house.
1.16.8.5.1.1. Con: Those people participated voluntarily.
1.16.8.5.1.2. Con: [Big Brother](http://bigbrothercasting.tv) is running a selective audition, while zoos just take exhibition objects according to race regardless of individual characteristic.
1.16.9. Pro: The rapid progress of biomedical technologies has led to the objectification of many natural entities, such as the fetus or embryo.
1.16.9.1. Pro: Also live stock, such as milk-cows, have more and more become milking-machines due to enhancement in antibiotics, hormone therapies etc.
1.16.9.2. Pro: Monkeys, mice and other lab animals have become mere testing grounds for medical, cosmetic and other applications.
1.16.9.2.1. Con: Animals were testing grounds in the 1890s as well.
1.16.9.2.2. Con: Nowadays, animal tests are much more ethical and are aimed to reduce suffering
1.16.9.3. Pro: Prenatal diagnostics,e.g. [Chorionic villus sampling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chorionic_villus_sampling), has enabled child bearing to become product selection \(admittedly on a very costly scale\).
1.16.10. Pro: With modernity '[Non-Places](http://www.acsu.buffalo.edu/~jread2/Auge%20Non%20places.pdf)' have been created that reduce the significance of place for humans.
1.16.11. Pro: Most people did not live with many family members around them any longer.
1.16.11.1. Pro: With increasing divorce laws more single households evolved.
1.16.11.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.2.1.14.
1.16.11.1.2. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.2.4.1.
1.16.11.1.3. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.2.4.
1.16.11.2. Pro: LGBT couples often have less children than homogameous male-female couples.
1.16.11.2.1. Pro: [LGBT's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_adoption_in_Europe) have problems adopting children. This makes it difficult to set up a wider family.
1.16.11.3. Pro: [Female fertility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Total_fertility_rate) rate decreased. This makes families smaller.
1.16.11.4. Pro: Around 1900, fewer than six percent of all [households](http://realtormag.realtor.org/daily-news/2015/05/22/single-person-households-are-rise) consisted of people who lived alone. By the 1990s, that percentage has jumped to over 20 percent.
1.16.11.5. Con: Single households are not a mere step away from "a natural state", they are also an [expression of women's emancipation](https://books.google.co.kr/books?id=no1MCgAAQBAJ&pg=PT1&lpg=PT1&dq=Single+Life+and+the+City+1200-1900&source=bl&ots=cfOHS1lnaC&sig=zweyhab5dgfAryGBaRF2eO1iFIM&hl=de&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjil9Doo5rMAhUGmpQKHWRKCTMQ6AEIQzAK#v=onepage&q&f=false). Not without reason is Virginia Woolf's essay on female empowerment titled ["A Room of One's Own"](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A_Room_of_One%27s_Own).
1.16.11.6. Pro: The focus was on the individual in the 1990s.
1.16.11.6.1. Pro: -> See 1.16.11.4.
1.16.11.6.2. Pro: People of the 1990s were seen as very hedonistic.
1.16.11.6.2.1. Pro: Techno, a very hedonistic movement, made its breakthrough as a widespread culture in the 1990s, manifested in the Love Parade in Berlin.
1.16.11.6.2.2. Pro: Musical genres like House and Techno as well as the introduction of new party drugs made clubbing more hedonistic.
1.16.11.6.2.2.1. Pro: In earlier times, many were dancing according to certain steps or remained seated. This ended with the advent of clubbing.
1.16.11.6.3. Pro: Religion was not as important anymore and so did religious communities vanish.
1.16.11.6.3.1. Pro: Sunday [Mass attendance](https://www.catholicculture.org/news/headlines/index.cfm?storyid=22222) in Germany is falling significantly since 1988.
1.16.11.6.3.2. Pro: The [relative number of Catholics](http://nineteensixty-four.blogspot.de/2011/12/yes-virginia-there-are-still-christians.html) in Europe decreased between 1900 and 1990.
1.16.11.6.3.2.1. Con: The [absolute number](http://nineteensixty-four.blogspot.kr/2011/12/yes-virginia-there-are-still-christians.html) of Catholics in Europe increased between 1900 and 1990.
1.16.11.6.3.3. Pro: Laws regarding contraception, homosexuality, abortions and women's rights were changed which indicates lessened influence of the Churches.
1.16.11.6.3.3.1. Pro: The Christian Church has been and still is a [strong opponent](http://www.catholicsforchoice.org/news/inthenews/VaticanEthicsGuide.asp) of science and technological, natural scientific advances.
1.16.11.6.3.3.1.1. Pro: The Church opposes the use of contraceptive medicines.
1.16.11.6.3.3.1.1.1. Con: Within the [Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_views_on_contraception#Dissent) there is major dissent against this opposition, so it is not very strong.
1.16.11.6.3.3.1.2. Pro: The Church opposes abortion.
1.16.11.6.3.3.1.3. Pro: The Church opposes cloning.
1.16.11.6.3.3.1.3.1. Con: The Vatican is not opposed to cloning in "[the vegetable and animal kingdoms](http://www.vatican.va/roman_curia/pontifical_academies/acdlife/documents/rc_pa_acdlife_doc_30091997_clon_en.html)".
1.16.11.6.3.3.1.4. Pro: The Church opposes inn vitro fertilization /  fertilisation \(IVF\).
1.16.11.6.3.3.1.5. Pro: The Church opposes the freezing of unfertilized eggs and embryos.
1.16.11.6.3.3.1.6. Con: The Church only opposes biomedical advances and not science in general. This field is special given its societal contestation.
1.16.11.6.3.3.1.7. Con: Many people oppose these biotechnological advances and the Church is merely their agent. Thus it is not the Church to blame but those principals.
1.16.11.6.3.3.1.8. Pro: The Church [opposes](http://stemcellresearch.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/11/usccb_2008-06-13.pdf) embryonic stem cell research because it regards this as "deliberate killing of innocent human beings".
1.16.11.6.4. Pro: [Marriage rates](http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/statistics-explained/index.php/File:Crude_marriage_and_divorce_rates,_EU-28,_1970–2011_\(¹\)_\(per_1_000_inhabitants\)_YB15.png) have decreased until the 1990s indicating that there is a trend to be more individual.
1.16.11.6.4.1. Con: A marriage can be understood as a strategic interaction between two individuals and, therefore, does not show the focus shifting away from the individual.
1.16.11.6.4.1.1. Pro: Individuals want to be married.
1.16.11.6.5. Con: The persistence of marriage as an institution shows that the focus remains on the couple.
1.16.11.6.5.1. Pro: Most women above 30 were married in France in 2006, which suggest that in the 1990s this [percentage](https://robertwhiston.wordpress.com/2013/08/28/46/) was even higher.
1.16.11.6.5.2. Con: -> See 1.16.11.6.4.1.
